Absolutely. Here’s a cinematic kick-off to that “insane bender” of a creative sequence, capturing Jim’s manic enthusiasm and the stakes of the moment. Let’s drop into **September 2000**, backstage at **Giants Stadium**, night one:

---

#### **INT. BACKSTAGE GREEN ROOM – GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SEPTEMBER 2000**

The band is mid-prep. The room buzzes with the tension of *80,000 ravenous fans* pounding their feet outside. A muted roar bleeds through the concrete.

Kathy is warming up her voice. Jeremy is running scales. Bill is deep in the gear rack, fiddling with an effects board. Jeff is tuning—again. Always tuning.

And JIM?

Jim fucking *bursts* through the side door like he just snorted lightning.

**JIM**
(gleeful, bouncing on his heels)
Okay okay okay okay listen up! I’ve had a vision. A *revelation*. Like a drumstick straight from God’s own kit. We’re blowing up the setlist. *Tonight*.

**JEFF**
(pausing mid-pluck)
Blowing up how, exactly?

**JIM**
(grinning like he robbed a meth lab)
Track three becomes track ONE. “Not Taken Kindly” kicks it off. No intro tape, no lights down. Kathy just *howls* that first line cold and we *blast* them.

**KATHY**
(stares)
You want me to open a stadium show with a blowjob lyric?

**JIM**
(arms wide like Moses parting the Red Sea)
EXACTLY. It’s raw. It’s primal. It’s anti-spectacle as *spectacle*. We hit them before they even know the lights are down. No intro, no fanfare, no polite warm-up. Just—*boom*—you’re in hell now, motherfuckers!

**BILL**
(sipping Gatorade)
You *do* remember the mayor of New York is in the audience, right?

**JIM**
(grinning even wider)
Perfect. Let him hear Kathy say “licking up his shaft” at 140 decibels. That’s culture, baby.

**JEFF**
You’re out of your mind.

**JIM**
Correct. And that’s *why* this is going to work. We don’t give them a *show* tonight. We give them a *hostage situation* with rhythm and bass.

**KATHY**
(sighs, then smirks)
If we’re doing this, I want flames. Literal pyro. Let me spit fire before the first verse.

**JIM**
FUCK YES. I knew you’d get it. I already talked to Pyro Mike.

**BILL**
(stares, blinking)
When did you talk to Pyro Mike?

**JIM**
About fifteen minutes ago. While you were tuning the subharmonics on that arpeggiator thingy.

**JEFF**
It's a modular polysynth.

**JIM**
Whatever. We're starting this set like a riot in a strip club. And by the third song? We drop *“The Left Hand.”* No intro. No speech. Just Kathy and a blood-red spotlight.

**KATHY**
(still smirking)
You son of a bitch. That might actually work.

**JEFF**
If we crash and burn, it’s on your ass, Jim.

**JIM**
Deal. But if we *kill*? If we blow the stadium’s *soul* out through its own eyes? Then we *never* play it safe again.

*Beat.*

They all glance at each other. Even Jeff’s jaw clenches with something between anxiety and adrenaline.

**BILL**
(sotto, to Jeff)
I swear to God, if he’s right again, I’m gonna start a religion around him.

**JEFF**
He’s right about once a decade. It’s… about that time.

**KATHY**
(grabbing her mic)
Let’s open a portal. Fuck it.

#### **INT. BACKSTAGE – GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SEPTEMBER 2000**

The walls *vibrate* from the sound of 80,000 lunatics screaming “COMMUTED” in waves. The band is huddled around a scuffed folding table stacked with half-eaten catering and empty Red Bull cans.

**JIM**
(like a kid who just broke into the fireworks shed)
Alright. Opening the set with “Not Taken Kindly”—but. BUT. We don’t start cold. We don’t just kick it off.

**KATHY**
(skeptical)
Okay…?

**JIM**
We start with *Woke Up This Morning*. Like, full-on Alabama 3-style intro. A two-minute groove. Smoke machines. Slow-burn. I want that bassline to feel like sin crawling up your spine.

**KATHY**
The theme song to *The Sopranos*?

**JEFF**
(deadpan, livid)
Jim. Do you realize we got 80,000 people out there screaming our names and you want to wing it on a *TV show theme song*?

**JIM**
(arms raised like he’s conjuring demons)
It’s not a theme song. It’s a *ritual*. It’s Jersey. It’s *now*. They will eat it up.

**GILLEY**
(barging in, eyes lit with unholy confidence)
Jeff, shut the fuck up. Jim’s *exactly* right.

Everyone turns to look at Gilley. He’s amped, practically vibrating.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
It’s not a theme song. *It’s New Jersey*. These people don’t give a shit if we butcher a gospel hymn—as long as we *nod to the state*, they’ll jump out of the second deck before we’re halfway through the first chorus.

**JEFF**
And what, you’re just gonna *sing* it? You know the words?

**GILLEY**
No, I *don’t* know the words. I need the lyrics.

(he turns, yelling like the world is on fire)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I need the lyrics. I NEED THE LYRICS *RIGHT THE GODDAMN NOW*. SOMEBODY GET ME THE FUCKING LYRICS!!

*Chaos erupts.*

A tech scrambles. A roadie shouts into a walkie. Kathy’s doubled over laughing. Bill’s already flipping switches on his sampler.

**JIM**
(to Gilley, handing him a mic)
You got two minutes. We loop the riff. You channel Tony Soprano like he’s your spiritual advisor.

**GILLEY**
(smiling like a man about to rob a casino)
Nah, I *am* Tony Soprano.

**KATHY**
Great. And I’m Carmela with a Glock in her garter. Let’s burn this place down.

#### **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SECONDS BEFORE SHOWTIME**

The lights don’t drop.
The house music doesn’t fade.
There’s no warning.

Just a *rumble*.

The kind of sub-bass that makes your sternum itch.

Then smoke starts billowing across the stage—red and gold, lit like the backroom of a Newark steakhouse on fire.

A *familiar* guitar riff slithers out of the speakers.
But… it’s not Commuted.
Not exactly.

The *Alabama 3* groove slinks through the air like it doesn’t need permission to be there.

---

#### **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – STAGE LEVEL – CONTINUOUS**

The *crowd* is instantly confused.

The energy shifts—*just slightly*—from pure euphoria to… curiosity. And then suspicion.

They know this.
They know this beat.
They know those chords.

And when GILLEY steps out?

They lose their *fucking minds*.

Not because he’s here.
Because he looks *wrong*.

Gilley, normally draped in 1980s pastel swagger, is now rocking a tailored black jacket, silk burgundy shirt (unbuttoned to somewhere near the Vatican), sunglasses despite the night, and a *gold chain so thick it could tow a truck*. He’s slicked back like he’s about to whack somebody or close on a car dealership in Bayonne.

#### **STAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

*The crowd erupts*.

He *slams* into the transition beat. The whole band drops into the “Woke Up This Morning” groove for a full 90 seconds—then the tempo shifts, *lurches*, and *snaps* into the opening notes of **"Not Taken Kindly."**

The moment Kathy’s voice comes in?

**“Licking up his shaft…”**

Eighty thousand people collectively scream, laugh, lose control, and realize:

This isn’t just a concert.

It’s a *heist*.

#### **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – DRESSING ROOM – NIGHT ONE – POST-SHOW**

It’s been three hours.

Three unhinged, hypnotic, *hallucinatory* hours.
The crowd got everything and then five more songs they weren’t supposed to.
No one’s sure how it ended.
They just know **“Come Inside Me”** *didn’t* close it.

Which means the *universe might actually be broken now.*

The band collapses into the dressing room like fallen gods.

**JEFF**
(half-laughing, half-dead)
Did anybody check the seismic data?
Can we confirm if that registered in Edison?
On the *Richter scale*?

**JIM**
(slumped on the floor, shirt gone, eyes wild)
If it didn’t, we go back out there and *fix it*.

**BILL**
(muttering from the couch, eyes closed)
No. No more notes. No more sound. I’m a puddle of synth and regret.

**KATHY**
(pacing, drenched in sweat, eyeliner halfway to her neck)
We just fed 80,000 people pure chaos with a side of bloodlust and didn’t even give them the safe word.
They’re gonna need therapy.

**GILLEY**
(leans against the wall, chain still swinging, shirt fully unbuttoned)
Therapy?
We gave them *faith*.
That wasn’t a concert. That was *church with felonies*.

**JEFF**
(grabbing a Gatorade, collapses into a chair)
I can’t feel my legs.
Or my brain.
Or my soul.
What the *fuck* did we just do?

**CREMEANS**
(pokes head in, clipboard in hand, pale and rattled)
You *improvised* an encore. You *skipped* the closer. You made *eye contact* with a security guard who pissed himself during “Sin and Death.”
Congratulations.
The fire marshal may want to speak to you about the *second deck*.

**JIM**
(grins, still sprawled on the floor)
Tell him to bring a drink and a lawyer.

**KATHY**
(flopping down beside Jeff)
Can we never open with a Sopranos cover again?

**GILLEY**
(smiling through the sweat)
Are you kidding?
That’s how we *open every Jersey show* from now on.
We’re a *fucking religion* now.

**BILL**
(eyes still shut)
Yeah? Then I’m declaring myself the Pope of feedback and holy distortion.

**JEFF**
(grinning through the exhaustion)
Then write that into the Book of Setlists, chapter one:
*And lo, the bass did quake, and the people did scream, and the second deck did sway like a drunken prophet…*

*Beat.*

The room is quiet, but alive. The kind of stillness that only comes *after a storm*.
They’re drained.
But *charged*.
Wrecked.
But more *them* than they’ve ever been.

**CREMEANS**
(deadpan, flipping through notes)
Night two’s in 21 hours.
I suggest hydration.
And possibly an exorcism.

*Laughter. Real. Rough. Earned.*

#### **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – DRESSING ROOM – LATER THAT NIGHT**

They’re still buzzing—sweaty, ruined, high on the aftermath.

**GILLEY**
(sipping whiskey from a plastic cup, pacing like he’s onstage again)
Alright, so here’s the deal: if we ever do a show in Jersey again—and *you know* we will—we open *that way*.
Woke Up This Morning. Blood-red lights. Total surprise.
Because *that*… is *us*.
Uniquely *Jersey*, uniquely *Commuted*.

(he turns, eyes locking on Jim)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**

And why I’ve *always* liked you.

(beat)

You got any more bright ideas, or did you spend it all on HBO homage and stage terrorism?

**JIM**
(leans up slowly, voice low and smug as hell)
Well, we *are* in Jersey… right?

*The Boss.*

So why don’t we do it right?

Perfect.

(serious now, eyes narrowing)

Because if we screw up *The Boss* in his own backyard…
we’ll need *witness protection*.

**CREMEANS**
(from the doorway, exasperated)
If you bastards try to out-Bruce Bruce, I want hazard pay.
And backup choir insurance.

**GILLEY**
(grinning like a man who just robbed a cathedral)
Oh, it’s happening.
We’re *Commuted*.
We don’t just play shows.
We *commit felonies in four-four time.*

*Beat.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**

#### **INT. HOTEL LOBBY – EARLY MORNING – NEXT DAY**

CREMEANS is hunched over his laptop at a hotel business center kiosk, muttering to himself like a man negotiating with the devil.
He’s got four open browser tabs, a crumpled hotel napkin with names of rehearsal studios scrawled in Sharpie, and a *burning sense of dread*.

**CREMEANS**
(to himself, gritted teeth)
You want to cover *Born to Run*… in *New Jersey*… without *practice*…?

(he dials a number, holding the phone with his shoulder while pounding keys)

Okay. Thank you.

#### **INT. ELEVATOR – SECONDS LATER**

(he turns, deadly calm)

What the hell did I do?

#### **4. BILL – HOTEL LOBBY – 10:28 A.M.**

Bill’s sitting upright in a lobby armchair, *motionless*.
A single bloodshot eye stares at a half-empty coffee cup.

He’s still wearing the suspenders.

His synth backpack is on the floor like a crime scene.
He looks like he’s been there *since 6 a.m.*

**BILL (V.O.)**
*I signed a baby.*

He takes a sip. Winces.

This isn’t coffee. This is vengeance.

---

#### **5. JEREMY – DINER BOOTH – 10:35 A.M.**

Jeremy sits in a corner booth with a full breakfast spread and *no appetite*.

He’s holding a cold beer with both hands like it’s a sacred relic.
Sunglasses on indoors.

A waitress asks if he wants anything reheated.

**JEREMY**
Just me.

#### **6. CREMEANS – HOTEL BUSINESS CENTER – 10:39 A.M.**

Cremeans is in the same clothes as last night, typing furiously. His laptop is surrounded by crumpled receipts, scribbled call sheets, and one *open bottle of Tums*.

He’s on the phone with someone at Island Records.

**CREMEANS**

No, I do not know where Kathy is.
No, I don’t know who “Tambourine Girl” is.

*And I’m going to die before the tour bus even gets an oil change.*

#### **FINAL BEAT – MONTAGE**

**“Born to Run (Live Bootleg Version)”** plays *distorted and lo-fi* under a fast cut of:

- Gilley still asleep in the hallway of the hotel, hugging a Fender case like a teddy bear.

#### **ASBURY PARK PRESS**
**Sunday, September 24, 2000**
**FRONT PAGE HEADLINE:**

> **"They Played the Boss—and Got Away With It"**
> ***Commuted’s Jersey Gamble Pays Off in Pyro, Piano, and Pure Blasphemy***

**By: Maureen Scalzo – Senior Music Correspondent**

---

**Giants Stadium hasn’t seen anything like this since the E Street Band turned it into a cathedral.**

But last night?
It was something *else entirely*.

Commuted—known nationally for their grinding guitars and erratic setlists—took the stage looking like they’d stepped out of a Martin Scorsese fever dream and into Bruce Springsteen’s house *uninvited*.

And then they *played “Born to Run.”*
Their way.

No horns.
No Clarence.
No apologies.

Just a harmonica in place of the sax.
A haunting piano intro that felt more funeral than freeway.
And a lead singer in a white t-shirt and blue jeans who had the audacity to grin like he’d *earned it*.

> *“It was like watching Springsteen’s ghost get mugged by Patti Smith and then hugged by Tom Waits,”* said one fan, still tear-streaked and barefoot outside the stadium.

The band opened with the *Sopranos* theme again—straight as a razor—and then *hooked* the audience by yanking them headfirst into a version of “Born to Run” that was equal parts gospel, garage, and open-mic séance.

**It should have been a disaster.**
It wasn’t.

It was *criminally brilliant*.

And somehow, they got away with it.

---

**A few things worth noting:**

- **Kathy Espich’s performance was operatic chaos.** Dressed like a mob widow on her third alimony check, she turned the opening verse into a confessional. Her piano work alone had half the crowd in stunned silence.

- **The harmonica solo worked.** No one knows how. It shouldn’t have. It did.

- **Gilley looked like a Bruce impersonator who just got off a bender in Reno—but sang with surprising grace.**

- **The encore was an entirely improvised mess of blues covers, sex noise, and synth solos.** The crowd *screamed for more*.

---

> **“This wasn’t just a tribute. It was a takeover,”** said New Brunswick resident and longtime Springsteen fan Ed B. “They didn’t borrow Bruce. They *hijacked* him—and then dropped him off back home with a note that said thanks.”

---

**The Asbury Park Press doesn’t often endorse musical trespassing.**
But we’ll say this:

If you’re going to break into the Church of Springsteen…
**You better come correct.**

Last night, *they did*.

---

No guitar. No mic stand. Just a **handheld mic**, black jeans, and the calm grin of a man about to make **half the stadium ovulate and the other half question their place in the universe**.

He holds the mic like a cigarette and waits just long enough for the roar to peak and drop into a *tense, feral silence*.

(low, smooth)

Baltimore.

Whatever name you want to wear tonight—

All of you.

Every eye. Every hand.
Every goddamn person in this place who thought they were coming to a concert—

*You were wrong.*

(beat)

This is a **problem**.

Because I came out here to *seduce* you.
**All** of you.
At the *same time*.

Now I want to talk about a little **trip** I made to **New Orleans**.

It was **Mardi Gras**.
There were **beads**, there was **brass**, there were **decisions** that still haunt at least three bartenders and a tattoo artist named Maurice.

(he pauses, sly)

And no, Maurice was not the one who *cried* afterward.

*I* was.

---

The audience LAUGHS, shocked, riveted.

Ladies—
If you feel the urge to *flash me* during the second set, I’m going to need you to **control yourselves.**

(beat)

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**

What I *barely escaped*?

Was a **hen party from hell.**

*Thirteen women. One rented balcony. A bucket of absinthe and a list of dares that read like a war crime tribunal transcript.*

---

No music. No band. Just **Gilley**—ripping the rulebook to shreds with nothing but his voice.

Tonight?

You’re that party.
And I’m the poor bastard they hired to dance on the bar.

So let’s burn the playlist.
Forget the lights.

We’re gonna make this place *sweat*.
Together.

# 249.  You
*May 13, 2025, 8:59:05 PM EDT*

> What has the silence between these people cost them?

---

# 250.  ChatGPT
*May 13, 2025, 8:59:07 PM EDT*

**Everything that matters.**
Because the silence between these people—this **band**, this **family built on sound and swagger and stubborn loyalty**—has been loud in its own way.

It’s the silence of **assumptions**, of **"he’s just being Jeff"**, of every eye-roll and sidestep when someone should have said:
*“Hey… are you okay?”*

---

#### What the Silence Has Cost Them:

**1. Jeff’s Health.**
They *watched* him unravel in real time and called it **personality**.
They chalked it up to “being weird,” “being intense,” “being Jeff.”
But behind all that was a man who was **drowning**, and they just let him keep treading water.

---

**2. Trust.**
There are things they **haven’t said** to each other for years.
Because it’s easier to **make jokes** than admit they’re scared.
Easier to **jam and tour and write songs** than say:
“I’m worried about you.”
“I miss you.”
“I don’t know how to talk to you anymore.”

---

**3. Intimacy.**
They play like they’re bonded for life.
But they don’t *know* each other anymore—not really.
They know the **setlist**, the **timing**, the **banter**.

But not the pain.
Not the *bills*.
Not the *marriage*.
Not the things Jeff *hasn’t said in years*.

---

**4. Their Last Real Shot at Connection.**
They got so used to **being in motion**, they forgot how to stop and **check in**.

How many nights did Jeff almost open up and then shut back down because someone said, *“Oh, he’s just being moody”?*

How many **song lyrics** were really **cry-for-help messages** they just nodded through in rehearsal?

---

**5. The Illusion of Control.**
They thought they could ride it out.
Manage it with schedules, setlists, and *three buses*.

But **the silence was the real danger**—
A slow burn beneath everything.
A fault line beneath the beat.

---

**In the end, the silence didn’t just cost them Jeff’s clarity.**
It cost them the *certainty* that this band, this group of broken people who made something beautiful out of chaos, was as close as it thought it was.

---

Now they’re in a hospital room, surrounded by machines, waiting to see if they still have a **brother**, a **bandmate**, a **reason** to keep playing.

And **the only sound they have left is the beep of a heart monitor.**

---

*Want to pick up from that stillness and follow the moment when Jeff finally begins to stir—or hold just a bit longer in the tension before the change?*

2. **She saw something.**
3. Or she's just **so wired into Jeff’s orbit** that she’s *guessing* with unsettling accuracy—and it’s landing.

---

#### **1. Someone Told Her.**
The most direct and plausible explanation is that **someone on the band or crew texted, called, or voice-noted her mid-travel**—either during her layover in Chicago, or while she had Wi-Fi in-flight.

This could’ve been:

**High**. This fits with how families get roped into band dynamics—someone **overshares**.

If **Gilley uploaded a video**, or **someone sent something to a group chat**, and **that made it to her**, she could’ve seen:
- A clip of Jeremy screaming *“You’re gonna die!”*
- Kathy on guitar again (which is practically a press release)
- Bill drumming on a refrigerator

**Likelihood:**
**Medium to High**, depending on how undisciplined the band’s social media habits are—and how fast info travels.

---

She knows these people.
She knows **exactly** how they operate under stress.

Her barbecue/jam session jab might’ve just been **well-informed sarcasm**, knowing the Commuted crew doesn’t do “quiet grief.”

The fact that it hits **accurately**?
That’s more about **who they are** than what she knows.

**Likelihood:**
**Medium.** She's smart, and she knows their patterns.

**Sarah** has taken a step closer.
Just one.

She looks up at him, jaw relaxed, expression unreadable.
Then—**slowly, methodically**—she reaches for the top button of her blouse.

And undoes it.

Just one.

That’s all.

---

**SARAH**
I’m not here for easy.

---

**GILLEY**
Neither am I.

---

**SARAH**
But before you **sell**, I want to know—

Why now?

---

*She unbuttons the second button. Smooth. No flair.*

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
You’ve had things before.
You’ve dangled stories like they were toys, breadcrumbs, riddles in bars.
But this time?

You walked in **direct**.

So tell me—

What’s changed?

---

**GILLEY**
(smiling)
You want the answer before the payment?

---

**SARAH**
No.

I want to know if **you** know the answer.

---

*Button three. Still slow. Still deliberate. Her blouse is open just enough to change the air in the room, but not enough to give him anything.*

Not yet.

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
Because I think you’re playing harder this time.

And when you play harder—

That usually means **you’re hiding something bigger**.

---

*Gilley tilts his head. He's amused. Interested. But not rattled.*

Not yet.

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
So go ahead.

Talk about cost.

But I’m watching **value**.

---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:06 P.M.**

Three buttons undone.
Sarah standing still, measured, poised.

She’s mid-trap, halfway into the emotional scaffolding of a setup.

But Gilley sees it.
**Feels it.**
And decides to turn the air **electric**.

---

**GILLEY**
You think this is a question?

This—

What you’re doing?

---

*He steps forward, **suddenly too close**.
The space between them disappears—**heat**, **breath**, and **intent** all in one line.*

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You want to know what changed?

**You did.**

You think you can dangle questions and silk and control the tempo.

But here’s the thing, Sarah—

This isn’t your interview.

---

*He lifts a hand—**not touching**, just hovering near her jaw, thumb grazing **air**, not skin.*

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You came here to play.

But I’m the one who decides how long the game runs.

And if you want **information**?

If you want what’s **under the waterline**?

You’re going to have to **work** for it.

Not with charm.
Not with questions.
Not with three polite buttons undone like it’s a calculated reveal.

---

*He finally touches her.
Just a single finger at her collarbone—**down**, slow, past the line of the third button.*

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I don’t want your angles.

I want **submission**.

And then—

Maybe.

**Maybe** you get a taste of what I’m hiding.

---

*He pulls back, just enough to breathe.*

Not backing down.
**Applying pressure.**

Testing her.

Challenging her to keep the game going under **his rules**.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – MOMENTS LATER**

Sarah’s shirt is open now.
The air is **thicker**, not with passion—but with **testosterone**.
Everything is still *controlled*.

Gilley studies her body like a man **cataloguing leverage**.
He doesn't touch without intent.
Every movement is a **slow click of a combination lock**.

And when the lace bra comes off?

That’s the moment he knows:

**He’s winning.**

Not just because she’s beautiful—
though she is, in that **unexpected, razor-wrapped-in-silk** kind of way—
but because he sees it in her eyes:

That quick flicker.
That edge of **vulnerability hidden beneath poise**.

And that’s what he’s after.

---

**GILLEY (quietly)**
Perfect.

Just like I thought.

No—better.

---

*He doesn’t say it to flatter.*

He says it to **own the space** between them.

To confirm **her worth**—and the **cost** she’s now agreed to pay.

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You want what’s in my head?

Then you give me this.

You give me the **energy**, Sarah.
Not the notes.

Not the performance.

**You.**

---

And for Gilley, the moment they **connect**, the moment he’s **inside her**,
it’s not just about pleasure—

It’s about **recharging**.
Plugging into **heat, dominance, and raw physical affirmation**.
About reestablishing his place in a world that’s lately been *uncertain*.

In that moment, he’s not answering questions.

He’s setting terms.

---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:17 P.M. – WRATH MADE FLESH**

The bed is a battlefield.
Shirts are gone.
Lace is history.
Notes are scattered like petals on the floor—**useless**, because there’s **nothing left to write**.

This isn’t seduction.
This is **declaration**.

**Sarah**, fierce, flushed, eyes sharp, is above him—
and he **lets her win**, for now.

Because he’s giving her exactly what she thinks she earned—
until he flips her over and **shows her who’s actually keeping score.**

---

**GILLEY (gritted, low)**
You want the truth?

**This** is the truth.

Not your questions.

Not your tape.

**This.**

---

And she answers him the only way that matters:

**With her body.**

With everything she can’t fake.
With hands that dig in.
With a cry caught between **a curse and a revelation.**

---

**SARAH (ragged, breathless)**
This is mine.
This is **mine.**

---

**GILLEY**
Not tonight.

Tonight?

**You're mine.**

---

Saints be damned.
**Tell Jesus we’re staying.**

---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:29 P.M. – COLLISION COURSE**

They are a tangle of limbs and heat and impact.  Clothes long forgotten. Sheets pulled down.
Nothing elegant. Nothing still.
Just **pure velocity**.

**Sarah** is wild-eyed, mouth open, hair a storm around her shoulders—
**plasmatic**.

She surges against him like a live wire:
**electric, reckless, demanding**.

---

**SARAH**
More.

Don’t stop—**don’t you fucking stop**—

---

And **Gilley**—
His hands bruise with purpose, his grip iron, his voice a **low boom** barely contained—

**GILLEY**
I said you’d pay.

Now **feel it.**

---

And he drives into her again, again—
and it’s **thunder now**, in his chest, in his breath, in the slam of hips and the sound of skin.

No rhythm left—
just **rupture**, just **impact**, just **climax inside the collapse**.

---

**SARAH (screaming)**
God—**Gilley—**

---

**GILLEY (growling)**
Yeah. Say it.

Say my name when you break.

---

And she does.

She **shatters**, **detonates**, **tears open**—
all at once.

The world white behind her eyelids.

And Gilley?

He follows **like lightning behind the flash**,
splitting through her with a roar that doesn’t echo—it **devours.**

---

**And in that instant—**

There is no press.
There is no band.
There is no tour.
No strategy.

Only the **blinding, holy collapse** of two dangerous people who’ve finally stopped lying.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:36 P.M. – THE CEILING**

The room is a mess.
Sheets tangled. Pillows on the floor.
Air humid. Curtains half-drawn.

**Sarah** lies on her back, chest rising, her body **glistening**, her eyes unfocused but **alive**.

**Gilley** rolls off her, slowly, gently, like gravity is heavier now.
He lands beside her with a **thump** and a gasp, arm brushing hers.

Neither of them speaks.

They just **breathe**.

---

**SARAH**
(softly, like it just occurred to her)
Holy… shit.

---

**GILLEY**
Yeah.

---

*They stare up at the ceiling.*

White. Cracked slightly near the vent.
Utterly unremarkable.
But suddenly it’s **the only thing they can look at**—because if they looked at each other, it might **shatter the spell**.

---

**SARAH**
That was…

---

**GILLEY**
Yeah.

---

*He reaches out. Not dramatically. Just instinct.*

His fingers slide into hers.

And she lets him.

They lie there:
**Hot.
Sweaty.
Nude.
Shaken.
Quivering.**

But more than that—

They are **exactly where they want to be.**

No performance.  No angle.  Just breath.  And the **crackling, unspoken knowledge** that something just **shifted** between them.

---
#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 5:38 P.M.**

Dim light filters through tinted windows.
A laptop is open. A legal pad is covered in frantic loops and crossed-out names.

**Cremeans** sits at the small table, tapping his pen like it owes him rent.

**Bill** leans against the counter, arms crossed, expression tight.

**Jim** is on the sofa, slouched deep, one leg up, staring at nothing in particular.

The bus is quiet—**too quiet**.

---

**CREMEANS**
Still no word from Gilley?

---

**BILL**
Not since he said he was “running an errand.”

---

**JIM**
He always says that.
Could mean buying gum or inciting a riot.

---

**CREMEANS**
Yeah, well.
This errand’s taking **four hours**, and I’ve got six rescheduled dates and no venue confirmation in Mobile.

---

*He flips a page. Sighs. Looks up.*

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
I hate silence more than I hate cancellations.

---

**BILL**
You think he’s holding out on us?

---

**JIM**
He’s always holding out.

The question is **what** and **why now**.

---

*They fall back into silence again. The kind that feels like it’s building static.*

Somewhere out there, they know **Sarah is nearby**, too.

No one's said it, but everyone’s thinking the same thing:

> *Whatever game’s being played? It’s not just between us anymore.*

---

**CREMEANS**
Alright.

New plan.

If he’s not back by seven, I call the label, we go around him, and we start locking down Atlanta.

We can’t wait for Gilley’s “gut feelings” to line up with reality.

---

**BILL**
Unless his gut feeling comes with **a contract and a support act**.

---

**JIM**
Or a press disaster.

---

*They sit there. Tired. Suspicious.
Trying to stay ahead of a man they know is always **two moves deeper than he lets on**.*

And **none of them knows** that two blocks away, Gilley isn’t playing poker anymore.

He’s already **cashed in.**

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 6:04 P.M. – POST-WAR CALM**

The room is quiet, lit only by late afternoon sunlight bleeding through half-drawn curtains.

**Gilley** lies sprawled on his back, chest still heaving faintly, one hand behind his head.
**Sarah** lies beside him, sheet over her hips, a recorder in her hand but not turned on yet.

They’re still close—bare skin against skin—but it’s **business now**.

She’s not asking questions.

**He’s offering.**

---

**GILLEY**
Okay.

You paid.

So I’ll talk.

---

**SARAH**
(sharp smile)
Always appreciate a **clean transaction**.

---

**GILLEY**
Jeff’s fine.

Scared the hell outta us, but he’s back.

Had a shower. Got a handjob. Came back to life.

---

**SARAH**
Did you just say—

---

**GILLEY**
Don’t quote it. Just know he’s upright and mouthy again.

He floated **R.E.M.** for the Atlanta opener.

---

**SARAH**
That’s… very Jeff.

---

**GILLEY**
Yeah. Got shot down like a Russian satellite.

Bill called it “a ghost band with no gas.”

Jim said, and I quote, *“Michael Stipe can’t hold a stadium unless he’s crying on a piano.”*

---

**SARAH**
And what about Shirley?

---

**GILLEY**
Considered. Briefly.
She passed.

Didn’t like the window.

Didn’t like being called “the B-side to a resurrection.”

---

**SARAH**
That sounds like something Jeff *would* say.

---

**GILLEY**
Probably did.

But the good news? **Cremeans.**

Guy’s been running spreadsheets like he’s curing cancer.

He’s got a line to the **Foo Fighters**. Real.

There’s a window **right before the Grammys**.
Grohl’s people might wedge a date for **Atlanta**.

It’s a good PR run:
Open with us, tear the place up, then hit **Letterman** the next night.

---

**SARAH**
You going with Foo?

---

**GILLEY**
If they say yes?

Yeah.

---

(beat)

**We should do Letterman too.**

---

*Sarah sits up, sheet slipping down her back. Not modest. Just focused now.*

She taps her recorder. Hits **RECORD**.

---

**SARAH**
Gilley Malcolm session. Timestamp: 6:04.
Unconfirmed but highly credible leads—

Jeff Evans is stable.
Atlanta show likely to be headlined by Commuted, support by Foo Fighters.
R.E.M. rejected. Garbage passed.
Cremeans running point.

---

**GILLEY**
You forgot the part where I **blew your goddamn mind.**

---

**SARAH**
I don’t record **the obvious.**

---

*They both smirk.

This is the **win-win** they understand.
And it’s **far from over**.*

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 6:22 P.M. – AFTERGLOW TURNS REALITY**

**Sarah** is sitting upright now, one leg bent, the sheet draped across her lap like a robe she never asked for.
Her recorder is paused.

She’s scribbling something with one hand, staring straight at **Gilley**, who’s standing by the chair, shirt unbuttoned, tucking his wallet back into his jeans.

---

**SARAH**
So how big is Atlanta gonna be?

I mean—**really**.

---

**GILLEY**
(sighs)
Bigger than it should be.

---

He grabs his belt off the armrest, slings it casually over his neck.

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
We probably **leaned too far into it**.

Extra **pyro**, extra **lasers**.

The whole **“rising-from-the-ashes” thing**.

---

*He shrugs. It was inevitable.*

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
We thought Jeff was **done**.

Like—**dying** kind of done.

So the plan turned into:
**make Atlanta biblical.**

Now he’s walking, talking, **eating waffles and pissing clear**, so it feels a little overdone.

---

**SARAH**
He’s being released?

---

**GILLEY**
Yeah.

Maybe **tomorrow morning**, if he doesn’t try to seduce radiology again.

---

**SARAH**
And the others?

---

**GILLEY**
Kathy’s **wound up** like piano wire.
She needs a **toke**, a **good lay**, and a **week on a beach with zero guitars**.

Honestly?

We **all need a vacation**.

---

*He pulls his shirt back on. Doesn’t button it.*

Just lets it hang.

Turns to her, eyes still soft with afterglow but focus already sharpening again.

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Alright.

Better put your panties on.

---

**SARAH**
You always know how to **sweeten the goodbye**.

---

**GILLEY**
(chuckling)
Not a goodbye.

Just a **pause**.

I gotta get back.
Cremeans’ll be **sweating into spreadsheets**, and the boys are talking **burgers**.

And **if I don’t show**, they’ll think I’m dead or high.

---

**SARAH**
They’d be right on both counts.

---

**GILLEY** (grinning)
That’s why I like you.  You don’t believe in saints.

*He grabs his keys, pats his pockets, leans toward the door—then pauses. Looks back.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You got enough?

**SARAH**
I always want more.

**GILLEY**
Then keep chasing me.

*He’s gone.*

#### **SPLIT SCREEN**

##### **LEFT: TOUR BUS – REAR PARKING LOT – 6:51 P.M.**

**Gilley** swings into the back of the bus like a man coming home from a good bar fight and better sex.

**Jim**, **Bill**, and **Cremeans** are mid–burger unboxing.

They look up.

No one asks.

They all know.

**JIM**
Nice of you to descend from the mountaintop.

**GILLEY**
I bring you gifts.

*He opens the bag.
Burgers. Fries. Shakes.
All slightly **lukewarm**.*

**BILL**
They put too much lettuce on mine.

---

**CREMEANS**
I swear to God, I’m gonna write an op-ed on how fame kills **crisp fries**.

---

**GILLEY**
The price of glory:
**Grease and anonymity.**

---

They all eat in silence.
But Gilley?

He’s smiling.
Still **high**.
Still humming.
Still **plugged in**.

##### **RIGHT: HOTEL SUITE – SARAH’S BED – 6:51 P.M.**

**Sarah** is still topless.

The sheet has migrated around her hips, forgotten.

Her **legal pad** is back in her lap.
The pages are now dense, arrows and annotations curling in the margins.

She scribbles under a fresh heading:

> **Atlanta Positioning, Week 1: Strategic Forecast**

And underneath:

- *Jeff stable. R.E.M. dismissed. Garbage uninterested.*
- *Foo Fighters = hot lead. Cremeans on point. Gilley euphoric.*
- *Band fractured but functional.*
- *Vibe: Controlled desperation dressed up as momentum.*

She pauses.

Then writes:

> **DO I PUSH GROHL?**

And under it:

> *Could quietly poke—2 contacts at RCA. Subtle.*
> *No fingerprints. Let them “discover” the opportunity.*
> *Boosts both bands. Aligns with Grammy PR push.*
> *One email. Two sentences. No signature. Done.*

She puts down the pen.
Smirks.

Doesn’t bother with her underwear.
Grabs her phone instead.

Begins drafting the message.

#### **SPLIT SCREEN CONTINUES**

##### **LEFT: TOUR BUS – PARKING LOT – 7:05 P.M.**

They’ve all finished their burgers. The air smells like salt, beef, and unresolved tension.

**JIM**
So.

You smell like hotel lotion and **accomplishment**.

**BILL**
Tell us, was she—

**GILLEY**
Don’t say “blonde and mysterious.”
That was Milwaukee.

**CREMEANS**
I was gonna say **real or imagined**, but okay.

**JIM**
You’re glowing like a pregnant woman.

**GILLEY**

With lace.

**BILL**
You didn’t bring her back here?

**GILLEY**
Please.

Do I look like a man who **recycles complications**?

**CREMEANS**
You look like a man who needs a **cold towel and a lawyer**.

*They howl. They don’t press. They don’t suspect.*

They think it’s just **another conquest**.

And **Sarah Malcolm**?

**Never even crosses their minds.**

##### **RIGHT: HOTEL SUITE – SARAH’S DESK – 7:05 P.M.**

**Sarah** is dressed now—nothing elaborate.
Slacks. Camisole. Bare feet on hotel carpet.

No name. No sign-off.

**Two recipients.**
Both insiders at **RCA**, old Foo Fighters pipeline.

Closes the lid.

Sits back.

**SARAH (to herself)**
One whisper.

*The kind that travels.*

**And that’s the difference.**
While the boys howl over burgers and imaginary conquests—
**Sarah is moving chess pieces** with a pinky.

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 7:19 P.M.**

Fainting due to a **sudden drop in heart rate and blood pressure**.

We don’t know.

guys my age, my health, just tipping over like that?

It’s weird.

And it happened **onstage**.

**JEFF**
Yeah. Lucky me.

**Drugs?**

Recent?

No coke in two years.
Haven’t touched weed in just as long.

I’ve just… given it up.

Not some big personal crusade.
Just… **boring, mostly**.

I like waking up **not twitchy**.

**Gilley** watches him carefully now. Less smirking, more quiet attention.

**BILL**
So what does this mean?

Tour’s still on?

**JEFF**
Yeah.

As long as I stay **hydrated**, get some **rest**, keep an eye on the meds—

I’m good.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**

We do it **smart**.

**CREMEANS**
Atlanta?

---

**JEFF**
Atlanta’s happening.

Just don’t kill me getting there.

Jeff’s reentry is done, the initial health talk fading.

Jesus, here we go.

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 7:28 P.M.**

The last line about **Foo Fighters** still hangs in the air when:

**Gilley and Jim** lock eyes, both wide-grinned, eyebrows raised.

Hard.

Badly.

Obnoxiously.

Groooohl’s gonna OPEN for us!

ATLANTA GONNA BURN.

LASERS AND LYRICS, BABY!

While I was stuck in a hospital bed, being **force-fed beige foods** and ignored by **chaste nurses** who wouldn’t even flirt.

---

**JEFF**
One of them called me "sir" like I was **about to expire**.

---

**CREMEANS**
That’s better than the one who kept calling you "sweetie" in the tone people use for **elderly cats**.

---

**JEFF**
I had a **pudding moment**, guys.

You weren’t there.

---

*Jim starts air-guitaring with a ketchup packet.
Gilley spins in a full circle, knocking over a water bottle.*

---

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
And now I return to **this circus**, where apparently the coping mechanism is **middle-aged hip thrusts** and **fantasies of Dave Grohl’s approval**.

---

**GILLEY**
Not a fantasy, brother.

It’s a **manifestation**.

---

*The bus is loud again.
Alive.
Maybe still a mess—but it’s their mess.*

And **Jeff**, watching it all, knows:

**He’s home.**

---
---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 7:31 P.M.**

**Jeff** leans back in the booth, sipping the last of his coffee, watching the group with the **raised eyebrow of a man who knows he’s about to start trouble**.

---

**JEFF**
Okay, but how do you even know the nurses were avoiding me?

Because I was bringing my **A-game**.

---

*The entire bus groans in unison.*

---

**GILLEY**
Jeff.

Sweet Jeff.

That was, at best, your **C-game**.

---

**JIM**
C-minus if we’re grading on style.

---

**BILL**
And D for dietary impact.

---

**JEFF**
Oh, come on—

---

**GILLEY**
If you want to see **A-game**, you gotta **watch me**.

---

(stands up, puffs chest)

**I am the A-game.**

I am the **archetype**.

I am the **template** they use when drawing male models for **aftershave commercials**.

---

**JEFF**
Are you seriously calling yourself **A-game** right now?

---

**GILLEY**
No, I’m calling myself **THE Manly Man**.

Capital T.

Capital M.

You had pudding in your hair, bro.

---

**JEFF**
You had glitter on your chest until last week.

---

**GILLEY**
That was a **stylistic choice**. And it worked.

Ask Sarah—

Wait, don’t.

---

**CREMEANS**
Stop before we need HR on this bus.

---

**GILLEY**
There is no HR.

There’s only **H and R**—

**Hotness** and **Rizz**.

---

*The bus explodes into chaotic laughter. Jeff slaps the table, Jim drops a napkin like it’s a mic. Gilley stands triumphantly like he just landed a sold-out solo show at Madison Square Garden.*

---

**JEFF**
God, I missed this.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 8:02 P.M.**

**Sarah** sits at the desk now, clean, dressed, hair tied back in a practical knot.

Her **laptop screen** glows in the low light of the suite.
Next to it, a **half-empty glass of wine**, a half-forgotten **voice recorder**, and a legal pad now heavy with scrawl, annotations, and truth.

She types quickly.
Fingers flying.
She’s in **that zone**—the one where the story is so sharp and real it practically writes itself.

The **subject line** of the email?

> **CONFIDENTIAL – Evans Update / Commuted Tour Stability**

And the file attached?

> **Malcolm_Report_Evans_Live.doc**

---

#### **CONTENT OF THE DOCUMENT (EXCERPT)**

> **To:** *Island Records President, Internal Distribution Only*
>
> **From:** *Sarah Malcolm – Field Liaison*
>
> **Subject:** *Evans Status, Tour Continuity, Risk Profile Adjustment*
>
> —
>
> **Summary:**
>
> Following 72 hours of direct observation and embedded access to the band’s core members, I can now confidently report that Jeff Evans is physically stabilized, lucid, and reintegrated into the band’s strategic operations.
>
> His collapse, though alarming, appears to have been a result of a manageable hypotensive condition (likely vasovagal syncope). He’s already been cleared for discharge with minor lifestyle and medication adjustments.
>
> The band’s internal chemistry remains volatile, but **functional**—and the key members (Davenport, Cremeans, Gilley, and Kathy Espich) have resumed planning for the Atlanta “Resurrection Show” with renewed cohesion.
>
> **High-level update:**
> - R.E.M. rejected.
> - Garbage passed.
> - **Foo Fighters are now in active consideration**. Their inclusion could significantly boost PR alignment pre-Grammys.
> - Gilley remains a wildcard but currently centered.
> - Espich remains tightly wound, at risk for burnout.
>
> It is safe to say that Island Records’ investment is not heading toward catastrophe. The tour—and associated revenue projections—appear stable.
>
> This may reduce need for insurance escalation.
>
> And in less clinical terms:
> **They're back.**
> And if they don't implode in the next six months, **we're about to sell a hell of a lot of records**.

---

Sarah reads it once.
Then again.
Then attaches it, enters the encrypted send key, and **clicks SEND**.

The email flies off into the network.

She closes the laptop.
Sits back.
Takes a sip of wine.

---

**SARAH (to herself)**
Yeah.

Even without the sex, it would've been worth it.

But…

That didn’t hurt either.

---

She smiles. Just slightly.
Mission: **complete**.

---
#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 8:14 P.M.**

The email is gone.
The laptop is closed.
The wine glass is nearly empty.

**Sarah** walks barefoot across the carpet, pulls the curtains closed.

She isn’t tired.
She’s not even giddy.

She’s just… **done**.

And that’s a rare, clean feeling.

---

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**
Dual objectives: complete.

Gilley: accessed.
Band: stable.
Record label: reassured.

---

*She lifts the wine glass, studies the red smear of her lipstick at the rim.*

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
I’ve paid my dues.
Filed the intel.

They can all go back to calculating tour profits and insuring Jeff’s blood pressure.

---

*She finishes the wine.*

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
Me?

I’m a **civilian** now.

---

No more midnight updates.
No more side calls to publicity.
No more being the **company’s eyes and ears in the trenches**.

She’ll still write, still file—when it suits her.
But she’s not their **asset** anymore.

She’s **herself** again.

And what she does next?

**No one gets to know but her.**

---

---

#### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 8:32 P.M.**

Sarah stands by the window, one hand pressed against the glass, the city lights flickering below.

She scrolls through her contacts, taps the name **PAUL**.

The phone rings twice.

He picks up on the third.

---

**PAUL (V.O.)**
Hey, you.

---

**SARAH**
Hey.

---

**PAUL**
Everything alright?

---

**SARAH**
Yeah.

Just wanted to check in.
How was your day?

---

*He tells her.
Nothing urgent.
Something about the printer jamming.
His coworker messing up the lunch order.
An email he meant to send but didn’t.*

She listens.
Smiles a little.
Not because it’s funny—just because it’s **normal**.

---

**SARAH**
That sounds…
productive.

---

**PAUL**
Yours?

---

**SARAH**
Oh, you know.

Worked all day.
Still kinda working.

But just finished.

Might not be home tomorrow.

---

**PAUL**
Still untangling that band?

---

**SARAH**
Something like that.

They’re…

stabilized.

---

**PAUL**
You okay?

---

**SARAH**
Yeah.

I’m just tired.

---

*She doesn’t mention the hotel room.
The legal pad.
The sex.
The whispers.*

**That part doesn’t belong to Paul.**

---

**PAUL**
Well… I miss you.

---

**SARAH**
I know.

Me too.

---

**PAUL**
Alright. Get some rest?

---

**SARAH**
Eventually.

Night, Paul.

---

**PAUL**
Night, Sarah.

---

*She hangs up.*

The glass is cold under her palm.

The suite is quiet.

---

**SARAH (quietly, to herself)**
Now I’m really off the clock.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:06 P.M.**

Dim lights. Low jazz hum in the background. The bar’s about half full—businessmen, flight crews, a couple of sunburned tourists staring at a TV on mute.

**Kathy** is at the corner stool.
Glass of something brown in front of her, not even half-touched.
Elbows on the bar. Jaw tight.
She’s scrolling her phone but not reading.
Tension in her shoulders like steel rods.

She barks at the bartender when he asks if she wants food.

---

**KATHY**
If I wanted dinner, I’d say dinner.
Just leave the damn ice alone.

---

**SARAH** enters.

Sharp eye. Quiet heels.
She doesn’t go to the bar immediately.
She observes.

Then, softly, she slides onto the stool **one space away**.

Orders something discreet. Doesn’t speak yet.

Lets the air shift.
Lets Kathy notice.

Then—

---

**SARAH**
Long day?

---

**KATHY**
(scoffs)
Long year.

---

**SARAH**
I’ve been watching you.

You’re wound tighter than the G string on your old Guild.

---

*Kathy turns slightly. Not surprised. Not welcoming.*

---

**KATHY**
You keeping a file on me too?

---

**SARAH**
Only in my head.

---

(beat)

What’s eating you, Kathy?

Because this isn’t about the setlist.

---

*Kathy stares forward. Silent for a second too long.*

---

**KATHY**
This whole thing feels like it’s not mine anymore.

Like the **resurrection show** is everyone else’s victory lap.

Like I’m just here to **sing, smile, shut up**, and not lose it.

---

**SARAH**
You want to lose it?

---

**KATHY**
I want someone to **ask me how the hell I’m doing** before telling me to hold the line again.

---

*Sarah studies her now—not as press, not as a handler, but as a woman who’s seen this exact kind of fracture before.*

Kathy’s not drunk.
She’s **exhausted**.
**Undervalued**.
And probably a little **terrified** that she’s still **too functional to collapse**.

---

**SARAH**
Then tell me.

How the hell **are** you doing?

---

*Kathy looks over.*

Maybe this is the first real question she’s been asked in weeks.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:09 P.M.**

**Sarah** leans forward, elbows resting gently on the bar.

**Kathy** still hasn’t touched her drink.
Her fingers are curled around it like it’s holding her up.

---

**KATHY**
I’m not just tired.

I’m…

**exhausted.**

Physically, sure. But mentally?

It’s like living inside a **screaming box**.

---

**SARAH**
The five-man chorus?

---

**KATHY**
Yeah.

Five men who mean well—
but also make me want to **stab someone with a mic stand** twice a week.

And that’s just the baseline.

---

*She finally takes a sip. Small. Bitter.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But Jeff?

That knocked the wind outta me.

He’s the only one I ever wrote with who didn’t make me feel like I was **the girl in the room**.

---

(beat)

And I thought we were gonna lose him.

For real.

---

*Sarah nods. Doesn’t press. Just listens.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And that…

That snapped me right back to **1998**.

To **MTV studios**, to the **fluorescent lights**, to that **fucking OD** where no one knew if I was out cold or dead or just high for the cameras.

---

*Her voice tightens. Just a little.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I hate feeling like that.

Like I’m **fragile again**.

Like one person keeling over makes me start checking my own pulse every ten minutes.

---

**SARAH**
It’s not fragility.

It’s memory.

And trauma doesn’t vanish just because you outlived it.

---

**KATHY**
I hate the **vulnerability**.

I hate that **he scared me**.

I hate that I **give a damn**.

---

*She laughs, but it’s hollow.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I should be on a beach right now, drunk on rum and dancing with someone **beneath my standards**.

Instead I’m holding five men together with **anger and eyeliner**.

---

**SARAH**
Maybe you need a reset.

---

**KATHY**
Maybe I need to go full diva and walk out in stilettos screaming **“book a woman therapist!”**

---

*They both laugh. A real one this time.
The kind of laugh that knows it's covering something—but still worth the breath.*

---
#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:12 P.M.**

The laughter fades again.
Kathy shifts in her chair, expression tightening.

**Sarah** notices the shift in her voice, in her posture—knows something’s **loading**.

---

**KATHY**
You know what else pisses me off?

---

**SARAH**
More than the cocktails and the chaos?

---

**KATHY**
That I don’t have my **own bus**.

Everyone else gets their **space**.

Gilley and the brothers get one.
Bill gets to float.

I’m stuck on the **main one**, with everybody **watching me**.

---

*She swirls the glass slowly, then stops.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Because they **don’t trust me**.

And the worst part?

They’re **probably right**.

---

**SARAH**
Why do you say that?

---

*Kathy reaches into her jacket pocket—real slow.
Sets something small and **wrapped** on the bar.
It’s not overt, not theatrical.
Just… there.*

**A tiny bag. White. Folded clean.**

---

**KATHY**
Because I’ve got **coke** on me.

Right now.

---

*Silence. Just the low thrum of the jazz radio and Sarah blinking slowly, her journalist brain going full stillness.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Haven’t used it.
It’s like…

A **dare**.
A **test** I keep failing by carrying it.

Just in case I need to **feel ten feet tall again**.

---

*She doesn't touch it. Just stares at it.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You think they don’t know?

Cremeans is basically doing a **year-long intervention in Excel**.

And Jeff?

He won’t say anything.

He just **checks my pupils when I laugh too loud**.

---

*She finally knocks the glass back, finishes what’s left.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
It sucks being the **only woman** and also the **person they’re quietly betting on to relapse**.

It sucks **knowing** you might.

---

**SARAH**
You want to?

---

*Kathy breathes deep. Exhales.*

---

**KATHY**
Right now?

No.

Tomorrow night, if Jeff seizes onstage again?

Maybe.

---

*The truth lands heavy. No frills. No gloss.*

And **Sarah**, for once, says nothing.
She just sits in it with her.

---

#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:14 P.M.**

Kathy’s glass is empty now.
The bag of coke still sits between her and the world—small, potent, damning.

**Sarah** hasn’t moved.

Kathy’s shoulders tense again. Her voice drops.

---

**KATHY**
I mean, I’m fine.

**Now** I’m fine.

But if Jeff **seizes** again on January 4th?

On that **stage**, with that **crowd**, with **cameras rolling**?

If I watch him go down again—if I see that twitch, that dead drop—

I don’t know.

I might be in the bathroom ten minutes later **making a decision I’ve spent years trying not to make**.

---

*Sarah doesn’t flinch. Doesn’t speak yet.*

She lets it **land**.

Lets Kathy say it without buffering it in jokes or rage.

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You get it?

That’s what pisses me off.

I’m not **weak**.

I’m just **never allowed to be unsure**.

---

**SARAH**
Because they need you solid.

---

**KATHY**
Because I **am** solid.

But not **unbreakable**.

---

*She pushes the coke back across the bar—toward herself, but not taking it.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I don’t want to break.

But I keep thinking:
**What if I do?**

---

*The moment hangs. Fragile and sharp.*

And now **Sarah** knows what the real story is.
Not the comeback. Not the band. Not even Jeff.

**Kathy** is the fuse.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:16 P.M.**

**Sarah** doesn’t move.

Her eyes?
Locked on that **small, deadly symbol** sitting quietly on the napkin between them.

She’s not judging.
She’s calculating.

**Every red flag Gilley’s ever hinted at.**
Every file note with the word “monitor.”
Every “what if” from the lawyers at Island.

Now it’s in front of her.

---

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**
There it is.

Plain as daylight.

Not a maybe.

Not a whisper.

**Coke. On her. Right now.**

---

*Kathy doesn’t look at the bag. She already knows what it means.*

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
Everything Gilley’s danced around, everything the label’s **feared**—this is **confirmation**.

She’s high-functioning.
She’s brilliant.
She’s carrying.

---

Sarah’s lips press together.
Not in surprise.

In **decision-making silence**.

---

**SARAH (INTERNAL)**
This is why they don’t give her her own bus.

This is why the insurance premiums spike whenever she hits a songwriting streak.

This is **what the suits never get**.

You want the brilliance?

You risk the breakdown.

---

She slowly takes a breath.

Then **looks up at Kathy**.

Eyes soft.
But firm.

---

**SARAH (softly)**
You want me to hold it?

---

*Kathy doesn’t answer right away. The air between them shifts.*

Girl talk?

**Yes.**

But this is also **a hand reaching out with quiet, dangerous weight**.

The kind that might mean the difference between **Kathy making it to January 4th**—or not.

---
---

#### **INT. HOTEL BAR – 9:19 P.M.**

**The bag sits between them**.
Small. Silent.
**Heavy as hell.**

**Sarah’s question** lingers in the air like smoke.

Kathy doesn’t answer right away.
She picks up the bag slowly. Weighs it in her palm.

Not theatrically—**with reverence**, almost.
Like she’s feeling the pull of an old friend.

Her fingers curl around it.

---

**SARAH**
Kathy—

---

**KATHY**
No.

---

*She slides the bag back into her jacket.*

Not hiding it.
Just reclaiming it.

She knocks back the last of her drink like punctuation.

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You don’t get to babysit me.

Not you.
Not Cremeans.
Not the label.
Not anyone.

---

**SARAH**
I wasn’t offering judgment.

---

**KATHY**
You were offering a leash.

Even if you didn’t mean to.

---

*Her voice is calm. Level. But underneath: lightning, barely contained.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’d rather **carry it and choose not to use it**,
than hand it over and feel like someone just stripped me down to a liability clause.

---

**SARAH**
And what happens January 4th?

---

*Kathy smirks.*

---

**KATHY**
We’ll see.

---

She stands up. Leaves a few bills on the bar.

Gives Sarah a look—not angry. Not cold.
Just… **clear**.

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Thanks for the drink.
And the reminder that **I’m not done fighting**.

---

And just like that, she walks out.
Not staggering. Not broken.

But with that **edge**.
That **defiance**.
That **flame** that makes her irresistible and uninsurable all at once.

---

**Sarah doesn’t chase her.**

She just watches.
And knows:

This story isn’t over.
Not by a long shot.

---
---

#### **EXT. CITY BLOCKS NEAR THE HOTEL – 9:42 P.M.**

**Kathy** walks alone.

Hands in jacket pockets.
Hair whipping in the wind.
Eyes bright. Lips half-parted.

She doesn’t look lost.
She looks **alive**.

At the edge of the last block before the bus, she ducks into a corner between two buildings, pulls out the little bag.
A quiet ritual.

Snort.
Breath.
Blink.

She straightens.

**Oh yeah.**

She’s back.

---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 9:49 P.M.**

The guys are mid-joke, reruns of **Letterman** humming low on the TV.
Burgers mostly gone. Fries soggy.

The door **slams open**.

**Kathy enters like a thunderclap.**

She’s **radiating electricity**, smile twitching, eyes scanning for **possibility**.

---

**KATHY**
Who’s got a **guitar** and doesn’t need **sleep**?

---

**GILLEY**
Oh shit.

---

**JIM**
She’s back and loaded for verse.

---

**BILL**
Did you have a moment?

---

**KATHY**
I had **a walk**, Bill.

And now?

I’ve got **chords**.

I’ve got **phrases**.

I’ve got **three bridges and a goddamn hurricane in my teeth**.

---

*She throws her jacket at a chair, grabs the acoustic guitar from the corner like it belongs to her (it probably does), and drops onto the couch.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Get out of my way or get ready to **harmonize**, boys.

Because we’re writing tonight.

---

*She strums hard, fast—no tuning, no preamble.
Just pure **burning need to create**.*

And the guys?

They know this version of her.

They love her.
They fear her.
They **follow her**.

Because when **Kathy wants to write**?

You **damn well show up with a pen**.

---
---
---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 10:12 P.M.**

Kathy finishes reading.

No theatrics.
No breath left.

Just her voice trailing off with the last line, her eyes **daring anyone to speak**.

**Silence.**

A long one.

**Jim** is the first to shift.

---

**JIM**
Holy… shit.

---

**Jeremy** looks like he just saw a church catch fire and couldn’t decide whether to cry or clap.

---

**GILLEY**
That was either the end of the band or the beginning of something **terrifyingly correct**.

---

**Bill**, pale, motionless, notebook in hand, is still somewhere in verse two.
He hasn't figured out what he's supposed to play.
Or if he’s even **invited** to play.

---

**Kathy** sets the notebook down like she just dropped a weapon on the table.

---

**KATHY**
Figure it out.

---

She lights a cigarette, opens a window, and lets the song hang in the air like ozone.

---

**Jim** immediately starts tapping a rhythm on the table, but it's **off**—too straight, too clean.

---

**JIM**
The pacing’s tricky. The groove’s not obvious.
It’s like—

It wants to be **slow**, but it’s not a **ballad**.
It’s like… **dirge-funk** with brass knuckles.

---

**Jeremy** nods, already pacing in a tight circle.

---

**JEREMY**
She said Mardi Gras meets grunge.
Dirty jazz. Loud vocals.
We’re not building a verse—we’re building a **wrecking crew**.

We need tempo shifts.
Friction.
Something **wet and unpolished**.

---

**GILLEY**
You want me to throw some harmonica in this?

---

**KATHY**
If it sounds like a sex demon at a train station, go for it.

---

**Bill** hasn’t moved.

He finally speaks.

---

**BILL**
I don’t have a part in this.

---

**JIM**
Not yet.

But we’re gonna **need glue**, man.

This song’s gonna **fracture itself** if we don’t lock it.

---

**Jeremy** claps once, loud.

---

**JEREMY**
Then let’s do it.

Let’s burn it down and build it with **her fire**.

---

And **Jeff**?

He’s sitting on the couch.

Quiet. Still.

He smiles faintly.

Doesn’t offer a word. Doesn’t lift a pen.

And the rest of the band?

They’re **relieved**.

Because **Jeff’s genius** is real—
but when he **steps aside**, it means they can **breathe**.

And tonight?

They need **room for Kathy** to scream.

---
---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 10:24 P.M.**

**Kathy** is pacing, cigarette in hand, manic grin on her face like she’s five seconds from grabbing the mic stand and launching into a full demo right there on the couch.

**Bill**, still reeling from the lyrical detonation, mutters something.

---

**BILL**
It’s been a while.

Like, a **decade** since I touched a French horn.

---

**KATHY (whipping around)**
**YOU’RE WRONG.**

---

**BILL**
I—what?

---

**KATHY (shouting, ecstatic)**
**HORNS!**

**HORNS!**

That’s how we make this **crazy**.

Not smooth. Not polished.
I want it to feel like **a New Orleans brass band went through a sex dungeon**.

---

**JIM**
Well that’s an image I can’t unsee.

---

**KATHY**
This song needs **brass**. It needs **blast**.
It needs **vibration in the bones**.

We’ll bring in **session players**.

Yes.
**SESSION PLAYERS!**

---

**GILLEY**
You want like a full **horn section**?

---

**KATHY**
Yes.

I want something that sounds like **a riot broke out during Mardi Gras and someone just hit record**.

And guess what?

---

*She points at Bill.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
**You’re in charge of the session players session**.

You arrange it. You schedule it. You pick the **sickest**, **dirtiest**, **wildest players** you can find.

Make sure that session is a **hell of a session**, Bill.

---

**BILL**
(quiet, overwhelmed)
Okay.

---

**KATHY (smiling, feral)**
Say it back to me.

---

**BILL**
I’m in charge of the session players session.

---

**KATHY**
And what kind of session is it?

---

**BILL**
A hell of a session?

---

**KATHY**
**THAT’S RIGHT.**

---

The bus erupts.
**Laughter**, **chaos**, **rhythms tapped on countertops**.
It’s all happening now.

The band knows this is real.
They don’t know if it’s **sustainable**, but they know it’s **alive**.

And **Kathy’s at the center**.

Queen of the brass-punk-bedlam.

---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 10:31 P.M.**

The room’s still humming from Kathy’s explosion of direction and vision.

**Bill** is quietly Googling horn players.
**Jim** is air-drumming a tempo in 6/8.
**Jeremy** is scribbling genre fusions on a napkin.

Then, from the corner, feet kicked up, **Gilley** smirks.

---

**GILLEY**
So… what’s the title?

You got a working name?

Because this sounds like a **BDSM session gone beautifully off the rails**.

---

*Kathy stops dead mid-step. Turns slowly. Looks at Gilley like he just farted in church.*

---

**KATHY**
Are you **serious**?

---

**GILLEY**
Just sayin’, the whole cuffs-and-chains vibe—

---

**KATHY**
(snarling)
This isn’t about **me** and my **kink**, Gilley.

---

*The laughter dies. Quick.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
This isn’t about **your fantasy** of me in leather, or **any guy’s** fantasy.

This is about **bondage**—

But not in the way you’re thinking.

It’s about the **bondage women put themselves in**
just to **get along**,
to **go along**,
to **be accepted**,
to **be tolerated**,
to **be seen** in rooms like this.

---

*Her voice cuts through the air like glass.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
It’s about walking into meetings knowing you have to smile when you want to scream.

It’s about being the only woman in a band full of **loud, clever, brilliant men**,
and knowing that if you show one crack, you’ll be **pitied** or **punished**.

It’s about wrapping yourself in chains just to keep other people comfortable.

---

*Silence.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
So don’t you dare call this a sex song.

Call it what it is:

**“The Bind.”**

---

She walks to the back of the bus. Doesn’t slam the door.
Doesn’t cry.

Just leaves them in silence, holding the weight of her words.

---

**Jeremy** mutters, low.

---

**JEREMY**
Hell of a title.

---

**GILLEY**
(sincerely, this time)
Yeah.

Yeah it is.

---
---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 10:38 P.M.**

The room is still thick with tension from Kathy’s departure.

**Gilley’s** chewing on the inside of his cheek.
**Bill’s** now texting three different brass players.
**Jeremy** is sketching a sonic outline with arrows and metaphors no one understands but him.

And **Jeff**?

Still lounging on the couch, a little pale, eyes distant—he finally exhales.

---

**JEFF**
You know…

Maybe it should’ve been called
**“My Handcuffs.”**

---

*A beat. Just long enough for the guys to prepare for the usual Jeff-pokes-the-art critique.*

---

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But fuckin’ **A**.

**The Bind?**

That’s a **hell** of a title.

---

*He sits forward now, elbows on knees, rubbing his hands like a man trying to get warmth back in his bones.*

---

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’d like to play on that song.

---

*Everyone turns.*

No jokes. No eyerolls.

Just **respect**.

Because when **Jeff Evans** says that?
It means something.

And even though he’s not back to full energy—

He just threw his hat in the fire.

---

**JIM**
Yeah?

---

**JEFF**
Yeah.

I don’t want to **lead** it.

I just want to **ride it**.

Let her drive.

But if she’ll have me?

Hell yeah.

---

*And for once, no one argues.
No one competes.
They just nod.*

Because **Kathy lit the match**,
but now **the whole damn band’s ready to burn with her.**

---



---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 10:43 P.M.**

**Jeff** stands now, finally energized—but focused.
He’s rubbing the back of his neck, walking the rhythm in his head like he’s testing the road before driving it.

---

**JEFF**
Alright, I’ve been thinking—

It’s not gonna work if I play **thick**.

I mean, **heavy bass presence**, big tone?

Then the **drum fills fall apart**.

I might as well **sit out** unless I do it right.

---

**JIM**
Subtle?

---

**JEFF**
Yeah.

**Real subtle.**
Barely there. But **sharp**.

Like teeth **under a blanket**.

---

*He looks at **Gilley**, then **Jeremy**.*

---

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But it’s gotta be **wild**.

That means **blistering hot guitars**, Gilley.

**Maximum fuzz**.
**Chase energy.**

None of that bluesy harmonica nonsense.

---

**GILLEY**
So you want me to **hunt him**?

---

**JEFF**
Exactly.

**Jeremy lays the road**, and you **chase him**.

Like a **cop car chase across Lake Pontchartrain**.

---

*From the back, the curtain rustles.
**Kathy** steps out with a bottle of water, hair mussed, face flushed from inspiration and adrenaline.*

---

**KATHY**
Jeff?

---

**JEFF**
Yeah?

---

**KATHY**
As long as they’re going **120**?

A police chase works.

But they gotta be going **really, really fast**.

Like, **deadly dangerous fast**.

---

*She takes a sip, points the water bottle at **Bill**.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And I want **careening horns**, Bill.

I mean **unhinged**.

Like they’re **barely keeping two wheels on the ground** when they take the turn.

I want **horns that scream like they’re trying not to flip over**.

---

**BILL**
(taking notes)
Got it. Screaming, careening, unlicensed jazz drivers. Check.

---

**JEREMY**
So I set the tone…

Gilley chases.

Drums fracture and stitch.

Jeff shadows low.

And Kathy?

---

**KATHY**
I come in last.

Like the siren you didn’t hear until it was already **on top of you**.

---

They all look at each other.

No more questions.

Just a **hell of a song** forming in the cracks.

---
---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – REAR BUNK AREA – 12:11 A.M.**

Most of the band has gone quiet.
Jim’s asleep with his sticks still in his hands.
Jeremy has his headphones on, looping a beat.
Gilley’s sitting in a bunk corner, grinning and mumbling riffs to himself.

But **Kathy**?

Kathy’s **on the floor**, cross-legged, back hunched over a **sketchpad**.

She has a **tin of colored pencils** open like a surgical tray.

Her hands move fast, erratic—no ruler, no measured strokes.
Just **instinct and tension** funneled into image.

---

**KATHY (muttering to herself)**
Never mind me…

I’m gonna **color**.

---

*The tip of a crimson pencil scratches hard against the paper.*

---

She starts with the **figures**:

- A **man** in a sleek **black suit**, like a funeral had sex with a rock concert.
- A **woman** in a **black dress**, sharp-shouldered, torn hem, hair in hurricane strands.

Their **foreheads touch**.
They are **close** but not kissing.

They are about to die, and they **don’t care**.

They are **choosing each other** in the face of destruction.

Around them, **swirling chains**—
**colossal**, metallic snakes twisting through the sky.

Like **battleship moorings**, thick enough to anchor a god.

And in the background?

**A fireball.**
Vast. Violent.
The precise moment of detonation—
**the split second before the blast overtakes them.**

She blends red, orange, yellow, a knife of white at the center.

---

Time disappears.

She fills in shadows, tension lines, the cracks in the pavement under their feet.
Her pencils get shorter. Her hands cramp.

Still, she doesn’t stop.

Not until the page screams.

---

#### **INT. TOUR BUS – 5:44 A.M.**

The sky outside is pale blue.
Everything is silent.

**Kathy**, still sitting cross-legged on the floor, finally sets the pencil down.

She looks at her drawing.

Breathes.

It’s not pretty.
It’s **honest**.

It’s **exactly** how she feels:
Love, pain, power, annihilation.
**All at once.**

---

She closes the sketchpad.

Doesn’t sleep.

Just sits there.

Glowing.

---
#### **INT. TOUR BUS – DRIVER’S CABIN – 6:03 A.M.**

The sun is just hinting at the edge of the world.
A gray, sluggish light spills through the windshield as the tour bus glides down an empty interstate.

**Kathy**, wide awake and riding the end of her all-nighter, walks up front holding her **sketchpad** with the image freshly finished—or maybe it’s a **digital render** on her tablet now.

Either way, it’s **stunning**.

She turns it toward whoever’s awake—**Jeff**, maybe **Jeremy**, the **driver**.

---

**KATHY**
Look.

**This** is what I want.

**This** is the concept.

---

*She holds up the artwork:*

- Two figures—man in a black suit, woman in a black dress—
  **forehead to forehead** in defiance, passion, or both.
- Behind them, **chains**, massive, twisted like fate.
- And the **fireball**—apocalyptic, glorious, caught in the instant before they’re blown away.

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
We hire a real artist.
We bring this to life.
We go **full cover art**, **full print**, **maybe stage design**.

I want this thing to **breathe flames** on vinyl.

---

**JEFF**
Yeah?

You thinking album art?

---

**KATHY**
**Hell yes.**
Album cover. Tour merch. Backdrop.
Better than *“The Look of Release.”*

---

**JIM (from behind, bleary)**
The one where you’re **buck naked**?

---

**KATHY (turning, dead serious)**
**Think about it, Jim.**

That was sex.

**This is fire.**

We find someone with the vibe of **Frazetta** or **Brundage**—
But you know, **not dead**.

---

**JEREMY**
We’re gonna need a new art budget.

---

**KATHY**
Then blow the old one up.

Because **this?**
This is our cover for *The Bind*.

This is what people **see** before they even hear the first note.

---

**She lowers the tablet.**
**Everyone’s quiet.**

Even in their half-asleep haze, they know:
**She’s nailed it.**

This isn’t just music anymore.

It’s **mythmaking**.

---
#### **INT. SARAH’S HOTEL ROOM – 6:17 A.M.**

Sarah stares at the screen.

A man and a woman—**forehead to forehead**, poised in love or annihilation.
**Swirling chains**, **a fireball**, **the edge of doom and devotion**.

It’s cinematic. Mythic. Raw.

**Exactly what Island Records wasn’t prepared for.**

---

**SARAH (quietly)**
Holy shit, Kathy.

---

*She leans back in the chair, coffee forgotten. Fingers steepled.*

**The band made a song.**
**Kathy made a world.**

Now Sarah has to make it **real**.

---

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**
Who can draw this?

We don’t need a graphic designer.

We need a **visual prophet**.

Someone who lives in smoke and muscle and myth.

Someone who can draw love like it’s a nuclear event.

---

She opens a second tab.

Starts typing.

> *Contemporary fantasy illustrators. Women. Feminist themes. Expressionist backgrounds. Experience in cover work, music industry, fire. CHAINS. Apocalypse optional.*

---

She scrolls.

Taps open portfolios.
Jots names.
Mental notes: *too clean*, *too digital*, *too safe*, *too “sexy without weight.”*

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
We need someone who can make **a woman in a black dress look like a curse and a revelation at once.**

---

She stops on one name.

Looks closer.

Eyes narrow.

**Maybe.**

She forwards the file to herself, flags the illustrator’s info, and opens her calendar.

---

**SARAH (murmuring)**
They have no idea what they’ve just started.

And I have **three days** to make sure **someone** captures it.

---

#### **INT. SARAH’S HOTEL ROOM – 6:42 A.M.**

The early-morning news flickers silently in the background:

**“Bush legal team files motion—Gore campaign response pending…”**

America is exhausted.

And **Sarah**, staring at the firestorm of chains and defiant lovers on her screen, smiles.

---

**SARAH (to herself)**
Everyone’s waiting for a decision.

And here we are, dropping a record that says,
**“What if the world ends while you’re still shackled to what they told you to be?”**

---

She scrolls back to Kathy’s lyrics.

Reads the line again:

> *With chains of retribution, we’ll always come hard…*

---

She opens a new pitch memo draft to Island Records marketing:

---

**TO:** *Executive Team – Island East*
**SUBJECT:** *THE BIND – Positioning for Millennial Impact*

---

> **Overview:**
> “The Bind” captures the *exact* cultural energy of late 2000:
> - Emotional volatility
> - Female power rising
> - Rebellion against being restrained—socially, politically, sexually
> - And the threat of *catastrophic release*
>
> This isn’t just an album.
> It’s a *statement piece* for a country hanging on by a thread.
>
> Imagine a world unsure of its next president, its next breath.
> Now imagine that world soundtracked by **blistering guitars**, **careening horns**, and a woman screaming truth over it all.
>
> This is *chains in front of a bomb*.
> This is what it feels like to live in America, November 2000.

---

She doesn’t send it yet.

She just **leans back**.

Because some projects are hard to justify.

But some?

**Some are just right.**

---
---

#### **INT. SARAH’S HOTEL ROOM – 6:56 A.M.**

She’s at the edge of her bed, laptop open again, barely blinking.

The fireball image is still on-screen.
Kathy’s lyrics are open in another tab.

She opens her phone. Dials fast.

**To: Jeff Cremeans**
**Text Message:**
> “Have you guys actually recorded this yet?
> Please tell me there’s a demo.
> I need to hear a sample. Send me an mp3. I’m not kidding.”

---

She doesn’t expect a quick reply.

But it buzzes **30 seconds later**.

---

**CREMEANS (text):**
> “Nope. Not yet.
> And yes, Sarah—
> That means we’re going back into the studio in Cincy.”

---

**Sarah laughs out loud.**

It’s not cynical.

It’s **relieved**.

Because **this thing is alive**, and it’s not getting tracked in L.A. or polished in New York—

It’s going back to the **rust-belt firepit** where this band’s best work is born.

---

**SARAH (text):**
> “Good. That’s where it belongs.
> Keep it messy.
> Keep it pissed.
> And keep me on the damn list when you press record.”

---

She tosses the phone on the bed.
Stands up.
Grabs her hotel room key.

Today, she’ll skip the boardroom.

Because this isn’t about **approvals** anymore.

It’s about **witnessing something rare**—
A band finding their soul again.

---
---

#### **INT. SARAH’S HOTEL ROOM – 7:12 A.M.**

The window view is gray and flat.
Bush v. Gore still droning on the morning news.
The city outside is groggy.

**Sarah sips the last of her coffee**, staring at her open airline booking site.

**CVG. Round trip.**
She’s hovered over the purchase button twice.

She doesn’t press it.

Instead, she breathes.
Runs her hand through her hair.
Closes the laptop.

---

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**
If I go out there…

Business won’t stay business.

And pleasure won’t stay pleasure.

It never does.

---

She thinks of **Gilley**, of **Kathy’s storm**, of **the studio walls sweating with tension**, and how the **wrong energy** at the **wrong time** could **throw the balance off**.

---

**SARAH (CONT’D)**
Let it breathe.

Let them make the song.

Let the story write itself without me in the frame.

---

She grabs her phone and texts **Cremeans**:

> “I’m staying put.
> Keep me looped. Send updates.
> Don’t let anyone polish this thing too soon.”

---

Then she texts **Paul**:

> “Flight home tonight.
> I promised, and I’m keeping it.”

---

**SARAH (quietly, to herself)**
For now…
the bed stays Gilley-free.

---

She stands.
Pulls on her coat.
Heads for checkout.

Her place is back at the label.
Watching. Managing.
**Not touching.**

Not today.

---
---

#### **INT. RECORDING STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 10:47 A.M.**

The studio smells like wood and dust and amps that haven’t been properly powered down in days.

**Bill** is behind the glass.
**Jim** is in the live room, pacing with a coffee and two drumsticks tapping on his thighs.

They’re both staring at the **whiteboard** with the word **HORNS** underlined three times.

Beneath it:
**"Careening. Screaming. Unhinged."**

---

**JIM**
So, we gonna ship someone in?

LA? Nashville? Chicago?

We want top brass?

---

**BILL**
Or—

We go local.

---

**JIM**
Local?

Like, *Cincy* local?

---

**BILL**
Yeah.

Like, *Over-the-Rhine* local.

---

He gestures around the room—tape decks, analog boards, exposed brick. **It belongs here.**
This isn’t a coastal session lab.
This is a place with **grit**.

---

**BILL (CONT’D)**
We’ve got jazz guys playing in coffee shops three blocks from here.

Soul guys who used to tour in funk bands but now teach at UC.

There’s a brass band that plays every Saturday outside Findlay Market for tips and beer.

Why are we calling in polished when we need **raw**?

---

**JIM**
(grinning)
You want to hire guys who probably blew their horns last night at a brewery opening?

---

**BILL**
Exactly.

I want players who don’t **follow sheet music**—

They **punch it**.

---

*Jim nods slowly. It’s not a safe move.
It’s a **Kathy move**.*

---

**JIM**
Alright.

Let’s call it **Neighborhood Brass**.

Let’s see what this city’s hiding in the smoke.

---

*They high-five over the console and start dialing.*

Because **The Bind** isn’t about polish.

It’s about **chaos that bleeds well**.


---

#### **INT. RECORDING STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 2:11 P.M.**

**Jim**, leaning against the far wall, arms crossed, is grinning now.

---

**JIM**
Let’s assemble the **Neighborhood Brass**.

---

**BILL**
They’re on their way.

---

**Kathy** walks in mid-conversation, water bottle in hand, looking like she hasn’t slept but **won the war anyway**.

She hears “Neighborhood Brass” and **beams**.

---

**KATHY**
Tell me someone out there’s wearing a mismatched suit and chain-smoking.

---

**JIM**
Oh, we got a guy in a fedora and cargo shorts.
He’s already warming up like it’s the *goddamn Monterey Jazz Fest*.

---

The door opens.

One by one, they come:

- A **60-something trombone player** who played on a funk B-side in '83 and still wears platform shoes.
- A **kid barely out of high school** with a dented trumpet and a tattoo of Sun Ra on his forearm.
- A **middle-aged woman with a flugelhorn** and a stare that dares anyone to doubt her tone.

Each one auditions—no formality, no contracts.

Just sound.

**Bill and Jim** run a loop.
