**Jeremy** throws chords like bait.
**Gilley** nods along, judging on **vibe**, not theory.

And slowly?

They start **building the horns Kathy saw in her head**.

The ones that careen.
The ones that scream.
The ones that sound like they’re about to fly off the track but **pull it back at the last second**.

---

**KATHY (quietly, to herself)**
This is it.

This is the noise I wanted.

---

#### **INT. RECORDING STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 3:07 P.M.**

The room is buzzing with energy and mismatched rhythms as horn auditions continue.
The chalkboard reads: *The Bind – Horn Section Scratch 2A*

**Jeff** steps into the control room, sunglasses still on, coffee in one hand, posture loose.

He glances through the glass at the next horn player taking a warmup lap.

Tall kid.
Trumpet that’s seen better days.
**Sun Ra ink** blazing across his forearm.

---

**JEFF**
Who’s the punk with the **Sun Ra tattoo**?

---

**GILLEY**
Just walked in off the sidewalk.

Didn’t even bring sheet music.

---

**JEFF**
Hire the fucker.

---

*The band glances at him.*

---

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I don’t care if he plays into a trash can.

**Hire him.**

**Hire him now.**

---

**BILL**
You want to, maybe, I don’t know—**hear him first**?

---

**JEFF**
Sure.

But if he sucks, we’re hiring him **ironically**.

If he doesn’t, we’re **putting his solo on the outro**.

---

The kid lifts his horn.
Nods once at Jim.
Count-in.

He plays **three notes**.

That’s it.

Not perfect.

But **spine-prickling**.

Unpolished. Real. A little wrong in all the right places.

---

**KATHY**
Yes.

---

**JEFF (grinning)**
There it is.

---

**BILL**
Okay.

Okay.
He’s got a bite.

We’ll shape it.

---

**JIM**
What’s his name?

---

**GILLEY (checking the clipboard)**
Says it’s—

“Spencer.”

Just **Spencer**.

---

**JEFF**
Good.

Don’t give him a last name.
Last names get egos.

---

*And just like that, the Neighborhood Brass gets its first frontline weapon.*

**The Bind** is one step closer to **sounding exactly like the apocalypse Kathy promised**.

---

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 3:29 P.M.**

The horn section is still warming up.
**Spencer the Sun Ra kid** is spinning slow figure eights around a groove on his trumpet.
The air is thick with feedback, brass, and coffee.

**Jeremy**, hunched over a synth, plugs in a fuzz pedal just for the hell of it.

He looks over at **Jeff**, who’s standing in the corner watching Spencer like he’s seeing a ghost from the future.

---

**JEREMY**
Jeff…

Are you trying to **summon Bootsy Collins**?

Like, what is this?

A séance?

---

Before **Jeff** can answer—

**KATHY** explodes from the far corner of the room, both arms in the air, hair wild, eyes wide like she’s just **seen God in a bassline**.

---

**KATHY (screaming)**
**YES!**

---

*Everyone freezes.*

**Bill** drops a pencil.
**Gilley** nearly spills a Red Bull.
**Spencer** stops mid-note like he just played the sacred riff.

---

**JIM**
Jesus, woman!

---

**KATHY (dead serious, breathless)**
That’s exactly what we’re doing.

We are summoning **Bootsy Collins**.

We are summoning **the funk ghost of the apocalypse**.

---

**GILLEY**
Did you just—

Did you just climax yelling that?

---

**KATHY**
It’s called **aesthetic conviction**, Gilley.

Try it sometime.

---

**JEFF (grinning)**
If Bootsy answers, we better have **an altar and a talk box** ready.

---

**JEREMY**
I got the fuzz.
You bring the holy water.

---

And in the midst of all this madness?

The track that started as **a scream of defiance** just found its groove—

**Possessed.
Unholy.
And ready to burn.**

---
---

#### **INT. STUDIO OFFICE – OVER-THE-RHINE – 5:11 P.M.**

**Cremeans** is hunched over a beige tower PC with a CRT monitor that’s humming like it’s dying.

The progress bar on the email attachment says:

> *Uploading… 2%… Estimated time: 41 minutes.*

---

**CREMEANS**
Oh my **Lanta**, this is horrible.

---

He jabs the keyboard like it insulted his mother.

**Jeff** walks past, sees the screen, laughs.

---

**JEFF**
What’d you do? Try to email the moon?

---

**CREMEANS**
I’m sending Sarah the first mix of “The Bind.”

**Six megabytes.**

And AT&T WorldNet thinks I’m trying to upload **nuclear secrets** on a telegraph.

---

**He storms out of the studio office and into the live room.**

---

**CREMEANS (shouting)**
Hey, **Bill**!

When the hell is your **landlord** getting **high-speed internet** in this place?

---

**BILL**
(turning from the board)
The **city promised** it’d be here **sometime before 2005**.

---

**JIM**
And that’s *if* the right councilman wins the recount.

---

**CREMEANS**
I swear to God, I could **walk** the file to New York faster.

---

**KATHY (yelling from the booth)**
Print it to cassette, slap a stamp on it, and pray.

---

**GILLEY**
Should’ve recorded the song directly into a fax machine.

---

**CREMEANS (grumbling)**
Next album’s gonna be on **floppy disks**.

We’ll just send Sarah the chorus and let her **imagine** the rest.

---

Everyone laughs.

The progress bar ticks to **3%**.

It’s agony.

But the file’s moving.

The song is **leaving the building**.

And soon, **New York** is going to hear **exactly what madness sounds like in Over-the-Rhine**.

---
---

#### **INT. STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 5:19 P.M.**

The PC still wheezes in the background.

**Cremeans** slams the mouse down and yells into the open air.

---

**CREMEANS**
Yo, bossman!

For future reference, tell the **landlord** to upgrade this prehistoric net connection!

---

**BILL (without looking up)**
Hey, bossman?

**I am** the landlord.

---

*The entire bullpen—**Jeff, Jim, Gilley, Jeremy, even Kathy from the booth**—**explodes** in laughter.*

---

**JIM**
Oh my God!

We’ve been **yelling at Bill** this whole time?

---

**GILLEY**
He’s been charging us **rent** to yell at him.

That’s genius.

---

**CREMEANS (grinning, mock-defeated)**
Okay, fine.

I’ll pay the rent.

At least it keeps it **in the family**.

But damn, Bill—
If we ever record something with **strings**, I want **a real internet connection** and maybe **a couch that doesn't smell like amps.**

---

**BILL**
Look—

I’m sinking a lot of my cash into this place.

Piece by piece.

It’s not polished.

Yet.

---

*He finally turns from the console, serious but excited in that **Bill kind of way**—measured and quietly visionary.*

---

**BILL (CONT’D)**
But one of these days?

It’s gonna be a **damn cool place** to make music.

**State-of-the-art**, yeah—

But with **vintage gear**, **soul**, and **weirdness** you can’t fake.

This room’s gonna have a **sound**.

---

**KATHY**
Like a basement full of ghosts and potential.

---

**BILL**
Exactly.

It’s gonna be a **snapshot in time**.

Like what the Beatles had at Abbey Road.

Tape hiss. Room bleed.
**Analog fingerprints**.

It’s not perfect.
It’s **real**.

---

*There’s a pause as everyone takes it in.*

And yeah—

It may be slow.
It may smell like burnt capacitors and someone’s lunch.
But it’s theirs.

And it’s **catching fire**.

---
---

#### **INT. ISLAND RECORDS – NYC OFFICE – 5:56 P.M.**

**Sarah** is seated at her desk, hair up, sleeves rolled, the skyline flickering beyond the tinted windows.

A message from **Cremeans** pings into her inbox:

> *Subject: THE BIND – DEMO 1 (EARLY MIX)*
> *Attachment: the_bind_demo1.mp3 (6.1MB)*

She clicks once.

**Progress bar: DONE in 4.7 seconds.**

---

**SARAH (smirking)**
Thank you, **T1 gods**.

---

She pops in her earbuds.
Hits play.

The track starts raw—no radio polish, no EQ smoothing—
just **Kathy’s voice**, bleeding heat over a rising wall of **horns**, **fuzzed guitars**, and **Jeff’s bass threading like a serpent** under it all.

By thirty seconds in?

Sarah’s eyebrows lift.

By the first chorus?

She’s not blinking.

---

**SARAH (quietly)**
They did it.

The crazy bastards **actually did it**.

---

She grabs her phone.

Texts Cremeans:

> “It's a monster. Don’t touch it too much.
> Let it breathe dirty.
> Also, good call on the kid with the Sun Ra ink.”

Then she sends another—to the head of A&R:

> “We’ve got a song.
> You’re not ready.
> Book a listen ASAP.”

---

She sits back.

Not smiling now.
**Focused**.

Because this isn’t just music.

This is the **sound of a band catching fire in a moment when the whole country’s about to turn upside down**.

And she’s got the **demo**.

---
---

#### **INT. ISLAND RECORDS – OFFICE FLOOR – 6:04 P.M.**

Sarah's walking back from her meeting with A&R prep when she spots **Josh**, a junior analyst from marketing, sipping La Croix near the water cooler.

He’s clean-cut, sharp, polite—the kind of guy who carries a Moleskine for note-taking, not doodling.

---

**SARAH**
Hey, Josh.

Got two minutes?

Take a listen.

---

She offers the earbuds like they’re charged with voltage.

**Josh’s eyes widen slightly.**

---

**JOSH**
Wait—this isn’t…

This isn’t **Commuted**, is it?

---

**SARAH**
(grinning)
It might be.
It might be **the song** they weren’t supposed to make.

---

**JOSH**
I’ve read the coverage.

Aren’t they the band that put a track called *Come Inside Me* on an actual album?

---

**SARAH**
Same band.

Different beast.

Trust me.

Just listen.

---

*He hesitates. Then puts one bud in. Then the other.*

**Sarah hits play.**

---

The horns come in first—off-balance, careening.

Then Kathy’s voice.
Like velvet **dipped in gasoline**.

The first verse hits.
Josh’s eyes twitch at the line *“Cuffs of savage foreplay, binding tight.”*

By the chorus, he’s frozen.

---

**JOSH**
(quietly)
Jesus Christ.

---

**SARAH**
Keep going.

---

He listens through the first verse and chorus.
Pulls the earbuds out like they’re too hot.

---

**JOSH (carefully)**
That’s…
That’s **really good**.

It’s also—

**That can’t go to radio.**

---

**SARAH**
Didn’t ask about radio.

I asked if it made you **feel something**.

---

**JOSH**
Yeah.

Like I should text my therapist and go buy a leather jacket.

---

**SARAH (smirking)**
Perfect.

---

She takes the earbuds back.

And as she walks off, **Josh** is left standing there, blinking, whispering to himself:

---

**JOSH**
What the hell *is* going on in Cincinnati?

---

#### **INT. RECORDING STUDIO – OVER-THE-RHINE – 10:36 P.M.**

The lights are dim.
Takeout containers line the counter.
The board is lit up with dozens of labeled tracks, and the mix of “The Bind” is hovering in the air like stormclouds.

**Kathy** is seated cross-legged in the live room, hair wild, eyes on fire, a mess of sketches, lyric revisions, and chain imagery around her like a ritual circle.

**Jim**, chewing a pen cap, leans into the talkback.

---

**JIM (tentative)**
Okay, hear me out—

What if we bring in **backup singers**?

Like—

Gospel-style. Big-band. Wall-of-sound.
We make it **insane**.

---

He pauses.

Dead silence.

Then—

---

**KATHY (slow, venomous)**
Hell.

**No.**

---

*The room freezes. Even Spencer the trumpet kid backs up a half-step.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
This is **my voice**.

Mine.
No harmony.
No reverb wall of echoing validation.

**No Gilley**, no choir, no gospel girls in red heels.

This is about the **power of a pissed off woman**.

---

*She stands now. Eyes like cracked glass.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
If you want gospel, write your own damn psalm.

If you want backup vocals?

Save them for the bonus track.

---

**JIM**
I was just trying to—

---

**KATHY (cutting)**
Jim?

If you try to dilute this with **hallelujahs**, I will **cut you**.

---

*Dead serious. But her voice is calm again.
Because she’s won.
She always wins when the art is in question.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
This track is going to sound like the last thing **a woman screams before she rips the chains off her ankles and burns the room down**.

We don’t harmonize that.

We **let it bleed**.

---

*Silence.*

Then—

**GILLEY**
I ain’t singing backup either.
Not after that.

---

*And somewhere in the control room, **Jeff smiles silently**, nodding to himself.*

---
---

#### **INT. STUDIO – CONTROL ROOM – 10:43 P.M.**

**Bathroom door slams.**
A moment of silence.

**Bill**, standing at the console, leans toward **Jim**.

---

**BILL (quietly)**
Does she seem alright?

---

**JIM**
Define "alright."

---

**BILL**
Like… seriously.
Has anybody actually seen her **sleep**?

---

**JEFF**, from the couch, doesn’t even open his eyes. Just speaks flatly.

---

**JEFF**
Nope.

She was sketching.

Remember?

While we were asleep.

Hell, I think she colored for, like, seven straight hours.

---

**GILLEY**
She *did* yell something about summoning Bootsy.

---

**JEFF**
And she flew in from the East Coast, right?

Like… **New York to Ohio**, then—

Down 70.
Hooked into 75.
Landed here.

**Then wrote all night.
Then recorded all day.**

---

*There’s a moment where everyone blinks and processes that.*

---

**JIM**
That’s…

That’s **a run**.

---

**BILL**
That’s **not sustainable**.

---

**JEFF**
It’s either **genius** or **the first ten minutes of a medical emergency**.

---

**GILLEY**
She did say she’d cut me.

---

**JEFF**
You’re not wrong.
She might cut all of us.

But only after the final vocal take.

---

*They all look toward the closed bathroom door.*

There’s no yelling. No movement.

Just the low hum of the console and the collective realization:

**They might be watching Kathy set herself on fire to finish this song.**

---
---

#### **INT. STUDIO BATHROOM – OVER-THE-RHINE – 10:46 P.M.**

**Kathy** leans over the sink, hands braced on porcelain, staring at herself in the mirror.

Her nose is bleeding. Not much. But enough.
Enough to remind her she’s **gone too far**.

The paper towel she grabs stains red before she folds it.
She keeps pressing. Keeps her breathing steady.

---

**KATHY (quietly)**
Shit.

---

Her reflection looks like a **goddess in freefall**—
Eyes wild, cheeks flushed, makeup smeared from hours of sweat and smoke and shouting.

**But the blood ruins it.**

Because **the blood is evidence**.
And if they see it, they’ll **know**.

And if they know…?

**She’s not the prophet anymore.
She’s the warning sign.**

---

She splashes cold water on her face.
Blows her nose. Checks for more.

Her hand trembles a little.

She grips the edge of the sink tighter.

---

**KATHY (muttering)**
Clean up.
Pull it together.
Do *not* walk out there looking like a punchline.

---

She opens her bag.
Digging fast—makeup wipes, concealer, lip balm.

She works in **tight, practiced strokes**.

This isn’t the first time.

She knows the dance.

---

She finishes.

Checks her teeth. Eyes. Smile.

Wipes down the sink.

Flushes the paper towels even though she knows she shouldn’t.

Then breathes.

In.
Out.

One more second of calm.

---

**KATHY (to her reflection)**
You're not the meltdown.

You're the **goddamn fuse**.

---

She opens the door.
And steps back into the studio—

**Clean.
Poised.
Lethal.**

Like **nothing happened at all**.

---


---

#### **INT. STUDIO – FRONT OFFICE – TWO DAYS LATER – 9:14 A.M.**

The **office manager**, clipboard in hand, stands stiffly in the doorway to the control room.

**Bill**, half-caffeinated, barely hearing him over the playback of “The Bind” track five, waves him in.

**OFFICE MANAGER**
Uh… Bill?  The plumber’s downstairs.

**BILL**(to himself)
What now?

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – BASEMENT / BATHROOM – 9:37 A.M.**

**Bill**, now trailing behind a gruff local **plumber**, watches as the guy pulls back from the open toilet with a wince.

The plumber holds up a **drain snake** coated in **soaked, mangled, blood-stained paper towels**.

He tosses them into a hazmat bag like he's done this before.

---

**PLUMBER**
Multiple **commercial paper towels**.  **Not meant** to go down a toilet.  Whoever stuffed these in here…They backed up the whole line.

**BILL**
Jesus. Is that—

**PLUMBER**
**Biohazardous waste.**  Look at the color.  Look at the consistency.  You got **blood in your drain**, friend.  I’m gonna have to charge **triple**.  Hazard gear. Disposal protocols.  You ever think about **putting up a sign**?

**BILL (under his breath)**
Not “No bloody nose cleanup in the toilet,” no.

**PLUMBER**
You should.

And maybe add **a trash can** that doesn’t scream “afterthought.”

**BILL**
Okay. Okay.  Just fix it.

As the plumber continues his work, **Bill stands in silence**, watching red water swirl in the bowl, and the thought hits him: This band isn’t just leaving a mark on tape.  They’re leaving it **in the walls**, **in the pipes**, **under the floorboards**.

---
---

#### **INT. STUDIO HALLWAY – 10:14 A.M.**

**Bill** walks back up the stairs, jaw tight, coat still unzipped from the cold air downstairs.

His hands are in his pockets, not for warmth—
but because if he doesn’t keep them there, he might **slam a door** or **shatter a coffee mug**.

**Jim** passes him with a mixer cable and gives a nod.

---

**JIM**
All good?

---

**BILL**
Yup.

Plumber's charging me **triple** for a **biohazard toilet situation**.

---

**JIM (laughing, not catching the tone)**
What, someone flush a raccoon?

---

**BILL (flat)**
Blood, Jim.

Blood and paper towels.

Women’s restroom.

---

**JIM (pauses)**
Wait… seriously?

---

**BILL**
Two women have used that room in the last 72 hours.

**One of them** has never touched coke in her life.

**The other** has a résumé that includes ODing behind an MTV set and then writing a hit song about it.

---

Jim’s face drops.

No punchline now.

---

**BILL (CONT’D)**
I’m not saying anything.

Not yet.

But don’t be surprised if the next song Kathy writes smells like bleach and denial.

---

They stand there.

Both of them knowing:
**Kathy’s fire burns hot.**
But they’re starting to wonder just how much of that smoke is covering **something about to explode**.

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – HALLWAY OUTSIDE CONTROL ROOM – 10:25 A.M.**

**Bill** and **Jim** are standing just a few feet apart.
The hallway is narrow, the walls thin, and tension **punches through the insulation** like a snare drum hit at full tilt.

---

**JIM**
So what then?

You gonna **cause a scene** when she walks in?

Because, look—
It’s your building, but—

---

**BILL (gritted teeth)**
I’m going to wait.
I’m going to see who **shows up**.
And **yeah**, we’re probably going to need an **emergency band meeting**.

---

**JIM**
“Emergency band meeting?”
You mean that **mechanism** we invented to vote on things like **setlists and stage lighting**?

This isn’t about **song order**, Bill.

This is **bitches using drugs**.
**Again.**

---

**BILL (snaps)**
Jesus, Jim.

**You don’t say it like that.**

---

**JIM**
Like what?

Like it’s **not** the third time we’ve had to wonder whether we’re gonna have to **revive her backstage** before an encore?

You want to be polite about it?

You want to **host a fucking brunch**?

---

**BILL (voice rising)**
I want to handle it like **a human**, not like we’re doing **goddamn PR for a meltdown**.

---

**JIM**
We’ve done **enough handling**, Bill.

Maybe this time?

We **cut the cord** before she cuts **herself**.

---

*The volume is loud now. Echoing.
People from the control room are peeking in.
No one steps closer. They all know the rhythm of a band **on the edge**.*

---

**BILL**
I’m not kicking her out without talking to her.

You want to be **a prick about it**, go ahead.

I’m going to give her a chance to walk in the door and **tell the truth**.

---

**JIM**
You think she will?

---

**BILL (quietly)**
No.

But I want to see if she tries.

---

They stand there, breathing hard.
No resolution.
Just **tension coiled in silence**.

The next voice that enters the hallway **might end it—or set it off**.

---

#### **INT. ISLAND RECORDS – SARAH’S OFFICE – 10:42 A.M.**

Sarah sips her latte, going over a release schedule.  Her desk is tidy. The windows are open.  **No fire alarms.**

**SARAH (to herself)**
No Gilley.  No drama.  No broken furniture.  Let’s call that a win.

Her calendar pings.
*“11AM: A&R Pipeline Roundtable.”*

She smiles.  Because today?  **Today she’s just a record exec.**  Not a **handler**, not a **spy**, not the woman **everyone expects to fix the band before it implodes**.

---

#### **MEANWHILE – INT. STUDIO – FRONT DOOR – SAME TIME**

The studio door opens.  **Kathy**, black hoodie pulled up, dark sunglasses on, holding a **coffee like it’s life support**, steps inside.  She’s been quiet for 48 hours.  No tantrums.  No brilliance.  Just… absence.  And she’s walking in like she wants to **ease** back into the room.  But **Bill is already there.**  Waiting.

**BILL (low, firm)**
Take off the glasses, Kathy.

**KATHY (flat)**
Good morning to you, too.

**BILL**
Take. Them. Off.

*Kathy lowers them slowly.  Eyes bloodshot.  Too much shadow under them.  Too much silence behind them.*

**BILL (CONT’D)**
You want to tell me what the **hell** happened in my bathroom?

*The hallway goes still.  **Gilley** looks up from his corner.  **Jim** stands off to the side, arms folded like he’s ready to throw down.*

**KATHY**
You’re gonna ask me this in front of everyone?

**BILL**
You flushed blood and towels and almost blew out the entire line.  You left a **biohazard** behind and didn’t say a word.  **Yes**, I’m going to ask you this in front of everyone.  Because **this is everyone's studio**.  And I want to know if you’re going to **lie** to my face.

*And back in New York?*  Sarah sips her coffee, smiling faintly at a well-formatted spreadsheet.  
Because she doesn’t know the fire has started again.  And this time?  It’s not in the booth.

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – CONTROL ROOM – 10:48 A.M.**

**Kathy** still has her sunglasses in one hand.  **Bill** is standing inches from her, jaw tight, eyes hard.  
The room is frozen.  Except for **Jim**, arms crossed, watching with **a fury he rarely shows**.

**BILL**
If you **used drugs** in my studio—On my property—You’re **done**, Kathy.  You're out.  You’re fired.
I don’t give a damn what you’re writing or singing.

**KATHY (snarling)**
**You can’t fire me.**  That’s in the **contract**.  **Non-negotiable.**

**BILL**
Then I’ll **burn the contract** and the goddamn board it’s pinned to.  This isn’t a label problem.  This is a **trust problem**.  You don’t get to bleed out in my bathroom and pretend we’re all blind.

**KATHY (shouting)**
You want to come for me?  Do it.  But don’t stand there like you didn’t know I was running on fumes and caffeine and edge.  You used my pain for **content** and now you’re shocked there’s a **mess?**

**JIM (exploding)**
**ENOUGH!**

*Both of them turn.  Jim walks between them like he’s stepping into a blast zone.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**
If she doesn’t get **help**—and I mean **actual rehab, actual doctors, actual detox**—I’m **done**.

**BILL**
Jim—

**JIM (cuts him off)**
No.  **Four o’clock.**  Press conference.  Two people from the **Cincinnati Enquirer** will show up—
And I’ll say it all.  I’ll **chuck the band**.  Say we couldn’t keep it together because **we let Kathy destroy herself in slow motion**.

*Silence. The weight of that hangs like fog.*

**Kathy’s face doesn’t move.  But her hand tightens on the coffee cup so hard the lid starts to crack.**

**KATHY (quietly)**
I’m not going back to **rehab**.

**JIM**
Then I’m not going back to **stage**.


*And just like that, the future of the band splinters in midair—Held together only by silence, stubbornness, and the clock ticking toward **4:00 p.m.**.

---
---

#### **EXT. OVER-THE-RHINE – SIDEWALK – 11:09 A.M.**

**Gilley** walks the cracked sidewalks of Cincinnati’s artsy, half-rebuilt district.
His jacket’s too light for the cold.
His phone’s been in his hand for ten minutes.

He hasn’t called her in weeks.

But now?

He does.

---

**SARAH (V.O., picking up)**
Gilley?

---

**GILLEY**
Yeah.

It’s me.

---

*He crosses the street, avoids a passing delivery truck, and stops beneath a rusted streetlight.*

---

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I need you to get on a plane.  From **LaGuardia**.  To **Cincinnati**.  Today.

**SARAH (quietly)**
…What happened?

**GILLEY**
The band has about a **fifty-fifty** chance of **dying today**.

**SARAH**
Okay. Slow down.

**GILLEY**
Bill found **evidence** that Kathy’s back on coke.  Like, hard evidence.  **Jim’s gonna quit** in **five and a half hours**.  He already said he’s calling a **press conference**.

*There’s silence on the other end.*  Gilley walks another five steps. Exhales.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
And I’m…I’m **considering quitting**, too.

**SARAH (quietly)**
Jesus.

**GILLEY**
Yeah.  So.  If you still care—if you still want this band to live—You need to get the **first plane you can**.  Because we are **right at the edge**.  And someone has to show up who isn’t full of ego, blood, or cocaine.

---

*There’s a long pause. Just breath between them.*

Then:

---

**SARAH (firmly)**
I’m on my way.

---

**GILLEY**
Thank you.

---

He hangs up.

And keeps walking.

Because sometimes, **even the one who jokes the loudest** knows when to call **reinforcements**.

---
---

#### **EXT. CINCINNATI STREET – 11:23 A.M.**

**Gilley** has stopped his pacing, standing under the flickering “OPEN” sign of a corner bar that isn’t yet open.

His breath fogs in the cold. His fingers tremble—not from nerves, but from knowing **exactly how fragile the band is** right now.

He pulls out his phone. Scrolls right past **“Jeff E.”**
Pauses.
Then taps **“Cremeans.”**

Because Evans?

Evans is **too wrapped up in Kathy**.
Too conflicted.
Too drained.
And if this goes sideways, **he’ll pour gasoline on it without meaning to**.

But **Cremeans**?

Cremeans is **a professional**, **a survivor**, and most importantly—

He’s the one who **got Kathy into rehab** after the 120 Minutes overdose.

---

**CREMEANS (V.O., answering)**
What’s going on?

**GILLEY**
We’ve got a problem.
A **big one**.

**CREMEANS**
Kathy?

**GILLEY**
Yes.  She’s using again.  Bill found evidence. Jim’s ready to quit. Sarah’s flying in, but it’s a courtesy call at this point.  And Evans?  He’s **checked out**.  Burned out.  Can’t even make eye contact with her.  So that leaves you.

**CREMEANS (quiet)**
How bad?

**GILLEY**
We’re talking **biohazard plumber** bad.  Toilet full of bloody towels.  Jim’s clocking a press conference for 4 p.m.  And if this thing snaps?  We’re not touring. We’re **done**.

*There’s a pause on the line. Cremeans doesn’t breathe loudly. He just **calculates**.*

**CREMEANS**
Where is she?

**GILLEY**
Somewhere between denial and collapse.
Coffee, sunglasses, looking like she’s got a hangover from outer space.

---

**CREMEANS**
And no one’s called her on it directly?

**GILLEY**
Bill’s *trying*, Jim’s *screaming*, Evans is *ghosting*.  You’re the only person she’s ever actually **listened to** in this situation.

**CREMEANS (firmly)**
Alright.  I’ll be there in fifteen.  No promises.  But if she’s still reachable?  I’ll reach her.

**GILLEY**
Thank you.  Because if this is how it ends?  It shouldn’t end like this.

*Cremeans hangs up.*

Gilley exhales, closes his eyes, and heads back toward the studio.  **Hope is a thin wire**, but he’s tossed it to the only person left who knows how to walk it.

---
---

#### **INT. CREMEANS' CAR – EN ROUTE TO THE STUDIO – 11:37 A.M.**

Cremeans drives through downtown Cincinnati, windows cracked, cold air creeping in.
His dashboard is cluttered with CDs, receipts, scribbled setlists, and an **index card taped near the vents** that simply reads:

> *“Don’t let them destroy themselves just because it makes great art.”*

He’s scrolling through old thoughts, half-remembered lines from books, liner notes, and backstage conversations.
Looking for the **right phrase**.

He’s done this before.

**One sentence.**

That’s what saves people.

Not a speech.

A **puncture**.

---

**CREMEANS (to himself)**
Come on… what do you say to the most dangerous person in the band who still thinks she’s the most important?  What would make **Kathy** actually stop?

He flips open his battered notebook.  There are quotes scribbled in the margins—his personal stash.  He mutters a few out loud:

**CREMEANS (murmuring)**
“You don’t get to be a martyr and a monster.”  No, too sharp.  “Talent doesn’t mean you get a pass.”  Too generic.  “Greatness doesn’t survive collapse. It gets buried under applause.”  Hm.  
Close.

Then—A page. Starred in the corner.  Written in his own hand, years ago:

> *“No one wants to play with someone they’re scared of.”*

He stares at it. Underlines it once.

**CREMEANS (quietly)**
Yeah.  That’s the one.

He snaps the notebook closed.
Turns onto the studio block.

Because now he’s ready.

Not to threaten.

Not to plead.

But to **poke the balloon** Kathy’s been floating on before it explodes.

---

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – HALLWAY OUTSIDE LIVE ROOM – 11:47 A.M.**

**Kathy** stands with one arm slung over her coffee, the other pushing hair behind her ear like nothing’s wrong.

But she knows.
She knows the energy has shifted.

Because **Cremeans** is here.

Not pacing.

Not yelling.

Just **walking straight toward her**, calm and still—like a man who’s delivered bad news too many times to tremble anymore.

He stops **twelve inches from her face**.

---

**CREMEANS (soft, controlled)**
Kathy.

You’ve got to go.

---

*She says nothing. Just a twitch at the corner of her mouth. Like she’s prepping a joke, a barb, a deflection.*

He doesn’t let her get there.

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
This is **rehab**.

Or this is the **end**.

---

*Her mouth tightens.*

She opens it.

He leans in **just a bit closer**. No breath wasted.

---

**CREMEANS (quiet, surgical)**
**No one wants to play with someone they’re scared of.**

---

And that hits.

It hits **hard**.

Not because it’s cruel.

Because it’s **true**.

And she knows it.

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
They love your voice.

They worship your fire.

But every time you walk into a room with your sunglasses on and your skin buzzing like a live wire?

They look at each other first—
**Not you**.

That’s not power.

That’s fear.

And it’s **killing** this band.

---

*Kathy doesn’t speak. She swallows hard. Her grip on the coffee cup tightens until it buckles slightly.*

He sees it.
The ripple.
The crack.

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
You’ve got one more chorus in you.
But you’ve got to **walk away first**, or you’re not coming back.

*He doesn’t ask if she understands.
He just waits.
Because he knows that if she’s still in there, **some part of her just heard it.***

---

> **"Am I embarrassing you?"**

---

**Jim** and **Gilley** freeze.  Because that’s not bravado. That’s **Kathy slipping**.  Not snapping back.  But **cracking open**, maybe for the first time in years.  And behind that one line is **a thousand fears** she’s never said aloud:

- *Am I too far gone?*
- *Do you still want me here?*
- *Do I still belong?*

And they both know—

**This might be the moment that saves her.**

---

#### **INT. STUDIO HALLWAY – SAME TIME**

**Jim** leans against the wall, palms pressed together like a prayer.

**Gilley’s** fingers are physically crossed, like **superstition has become survival instinct**.

They look at each other when they hear her say it.

---

**KATHY (O.S.)**
Am I embarrassing you?

---

**GILLEY (softly)**
Oh shit.

That’s the voice.

---

**JIM (low)**
That’s not a wall.

That’s…

That’s a door.

---

*They don’t move.
They don’t interrupt.
They just stand there, hearts thudding, waiting to see if **she walks through it.***

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – OUTER HALLWAY – 11:50 A.M.**

**Cremeans** doesn’t move at first.
He lets her question hang in the air—fragile, uncertain.

She’s not yelling.
She’s not storming out.

She’s *asking*.

And that’s more honest than anything she’s said in weeks.

---

**CREMEANS (gently)**
No.

You’re not embarrassing me.

You’re **scaring me**.

---

*Kathy’s jaw shifts. Just slightly. Like the words hit but she’s not sure what to do with them yet.*

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
You think you’re the problem?

You’re not.

But you’ve become **the danger**.

To yourself.
To the people who love you.
To the music.

---

*Her hands tremble around her coffee cup. She doesn’t meet his eyes, but she doesn’t walk away either.*

---

**CREMEANS (lower)**
This isn’t about shame.

This is about whether you still want to be **in this**—
Alive.
Real.
Creating.

Or if you’re just **trying to go out in flames and call it legacy**.

---

*Kathy closes her eyes.
The sunglasses are tucked into her hoodie now, forgotten.
She leans her head back against the wall behind her.*

---

**KATHY (barely audible)**
I don’t know how to stop without disappearing.

---

**CREMEANS (softer still)**
Then don’t disappear.

**Let someone carry you for a while.**

Let us help you come back.

---

*For the first time in what feels like forever—Kathy says nothing.
But she nods.
Once.
Barely.*

And that’s enough.

That’s the needle.

That’s the puncture.

---

#### **INT. STUDIO – HALLWAY – 11:53 A.M.**

**Cremeans**, still steady, still close, offers his quiet truth:


**CREMEANS**
We did the same thing for **Jeff** last week.

You were there for him.

Let us do that for **you**.

---

*Kathy doesn’t react at first.
Then slowly—she nods once.*

But not all the way.

---

**KATHY (softly)**
Yeah.

But I mean…
**us**.

As in…

**Everyone but Jeff.**

---

*Cremeans tilts his head. Gently prodding, no judgment.*

---

**CREMEANS**
Why?

What’s between you two right now?

---

**KATHY**
Nothing.

And **that’s the problem**.

---

*She exhales. The first real one in minutes.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’ve **embarrassed him**.

I don’t want to face it.
Not yet.

Because if we keep writing the way we’ve written—
If we keep building these **wicked, blistering tunes** like we’ve been doing for a decade—

And I **throw it all away**?

I’m not just burning out.

I’m **betraying him**.

---

*She leans against the wall. Not collapsing—just softening. Like someone finally admitting what’s been chewing at them from the inside.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
What good is a **partnership** if the partner doesn’t **contribute**?

What’s the point of having a **twin engine** when one just **shuts off midair**?

---

*Cremeans doesn’t fill the silence. He gives her space to live in it.*

Then he speaks—**carefully**, like threading a needle through a vein.

---

**CREMEANS**
You *are* contributing.

You always have.

But if you go down now—
You’re not just leaving Jeff behind.

You’re taking the **whole engine** with you.

---

*Kathy presses the heel of her hand to her eye.*

A tear doesn’t fall.
But it almost does.

---

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Let us help you land the plane, Kath.

Then you can face him.
With your music.
With your words.

Not with **an apology**…

With a **track so good it forgives you first.**

---

*And for the first time, Kathy lets her head hang forward.
Not out of shame.

Out of relief.
Of letting the armor fall.*

---

**KATHY (barely audible)**
Okay.

---

#### **INT. CREMEANS’ OFFICE – STUDIO – 12:02 P.M.**

It’s the only space in the building with:

- A **leather chair** that doesn’t creak.
- A **water cooler** that actually works.
- A **locked door** and no band posters.

It smells like **paperwork, strategy, and quiet panic**.

**Kathy** slumps into the chair, not in collapse, but in **acceptance**.
She sips from a Styrofoam cup of water and doesn’t argue.

---

**CREMEANS**
You’re staying here.
You breathe.
You don’t answer questions.

And you don’t explain anything to anyone yet.

Not until **you’re ready**.

---

*Kathy nods once.*

---

**KATHY**
Thank you.

---

**CREMEANS (gently)**
Thank me when you’re better.

---

He closes the door behind him with quiet finality.

Then he turns to the hallway.

And what walks out isn’t the negotiator anymore.
It’s the **field commander**.

---

#### **INT. STUDIO HALLWAY – SECONDS LATER**

**Jim**, still pacing. **Gilley**, on edge. The air’s like glass.

Cremeans emerges and holds up a hand before they even ask.

---

**CREMEANS**
She’s in my office.

Door’s closed.
Air’s on.
She’s drinking water and not spiraling.

They nod, barely.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Now listen to me, both of you.

If you see **Jeff** or **Jeremy** walk through that door?

**Not. A. God-blessed. Word.**

**JIM**
We weren’t gonna—


**CREMEANS (cutting him off)**
**Not a word.**

Not a look.
Not a sigh.
Not a passive-aggressive mutter that sounds like a bassline.

She is **one sentence away from walking out** and never coming back.

You let me manage this.


**GILLEY (softly)**
Okay, boss.


Cremeans nods once.

Sharp. Measured.

Then heads down the hall, already bracing for **Evans**, **Jeremy**, or **reality** to blow it all open.

---
---

#### **INT. CREMEANS’ OFFICE – 12:08 P.M.**

The **leather chair** creaks softly as **Kathy shifts**, knees pulled up, arms curled around the Styrofoam cup of water.

The hum of the water cooler is the only sound in the room.

Her sunglasses sit on the desk, discarded.

Her face is raw, tired—more human than rockstar.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
What the fuck is wrong with me?

I just detonated a band built on fifteen years of sweat and lightning…

For what?

For a **line in the dark**?

---

She stares at the water like it's a confessional.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
This wasn’t even epic.
It was just **stupid**.

The worst kind of stupid.

The kind that feels good for five minutes
and ruins **everything** for five years.

---

She leans her head back.

Watches the ceiling.

Eyes blinking slowly.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
And the worst part?

The part no one wants to hear?

I’m gonna **miss it**.

I already do.

She presses the cold cup to her forehead.

**KATHY (internal)**
Jesus Christ, Eric Clapton makes more sense to me now than he ever did when I was sober.

*If you wanna hang out, you’ve gotta take her out… cocaine.*

Yeah.

**Exactly, Eric.**

She laughs. Once. Bitter.

Then she stops.

And just sits.

Because **this is the hardest part**.

Not the detox.
Not the questions.
Not even the judgment.

It’s **missing the thing that almost killed you**
and knowing you’ll **miss it again tomorrow.**

---
---

#### **CREMEANS’ OFFICE – MOMENTS EARLIER**

The leather chair squeaks as Kathy shifts.
Her legs are pulled up, her coffee gone cold.

On the desk: a **legal pad** half-filled with her handwriting.

Bold. Unflinching. Messy where the pen dragged through sudden, urgent phrases.

The lyrics are brutal:

> *The back of my throat, a sacrificial shrine,
> Thrusts deep within, crossing all of my lines.*

And raw:

> *We stare into the abyss, can you feel the heat?
> Caught in a twister, where desire meets.*

And aching:

> *Tomorrow may ache, but tonight we're alive,
> In this realm of madness, together we thrive.*

It’s **Kathy’s heart**, laid bare in ink.

---

#### **DOOR OPENS – CREMEANS ENTERS**

**CREMEANS**
Let’s go.

---

She nods.

No protest.
No smile.
Just tired, willing surrender.

She gets up.

The pad stays.

Cremeans doesn’t see it right away.

But when he does—
He’ll know what it is.

He’ll know what she left behind.

Not just a song.

But the moment **she cracked.**

---
---

#### **INT. BILL’S STUDIO – CREMEANS’ COURTESY OFFICE – DAY 21**

The leather chair creaks from disuse.
The water cooler hums with one-third its original strength.

**Cremeans** pushes open the door, looking for a folder he thinks he left behind.

Instead, he finds **a yellow legal pad**, half-covered by a stack of mix notes.

The handwriting is unmistakable.

**Kathy.**

---

**CREMEANS (to himself)**
Shit.

---

He sits down.
Opens the pad.
And reads.

It hits hard.

It’s not just lyrics.
It’s a **purge**.
A journal.
A confession dressed in meter and metaphor.

Some of it’s nearly illegible from where the pen gouged the page.

Lines like knives:

> *The mirror cracked, I kissed the edge,
> Left blood like lipstick on the pledge.*

> *He watches me unravel, doesn't blink—
> My body's a roadmap, cocaine for ink.*

> *I missed the bruise that told the truth,
> Still danced like pain was just my proof.*

Cremeans puts the pad down slowly.

The room is too quiet now.

---

**CREMEANS (quiet)**
Goddamn.

---

He knows what this is.

**Not a song.
Not yet.**

It’s what she couldn’t say.
What she needed to leave behind.
What she *couldn’t carry* into recovery.

And now?

It’s his.

To protect.
To maybe shape.
To maybe give back to her—when she’s ready.

---

#### **INT. BILL’S STUDIO – COURTESY OFFICE – DAY 21, LATE AFTERNOON**

**Cremeans** sits with the legal pad open in front of him, its weight **far greater than the page count**.

He stares at it like it might **ignite**.

---

**CREMEANS (muttering)**
What the hell am I supposed to do with this?

I’m an **SAP consultant** who got stuck managing a band full of firecrackers.

I count money, not meltdowns.

---

He flips through a few more pages.

Every line is either **unrecordable**, **unreleasable**, or **completely brilliant**.

Definitely **not safe in the hands of anyone who’d use it recklessly**.

He looks at his contacts list.

And strikes names off one by one:

- **Jeff Evans?** In **London**, pretending not to care.
- **Jeremy?** On a beach in **Rio**, probably shirtless and sipping sugarcane cocktails.
- **Jim?** In **Springboro**, knee-deep in his hometown's Holiday Parade and probably arguing about float logistics.
- **Gilley?** In **L.A.**, doing… Gilley things. Most likely **thinking with his zipper**.

That leaves one person:

**Bill.**

Because **Bill is local.
Bill is steady.
Bill has been there since day one.**

And **Bill isn’t afraid** of what Kathy sounds like **when she’s dangerous**.

---

**CREMEANS (grabbing his phone)**
Okay, Bill.

Tag in.

---

He dials.

---

**CREMEANS (into phone)**
Hey, when you get here—I’ve got something.

No rush.
But, like… yeah.

**It's Kathy.**

And it’s a lot.

---
---

#### **INT. REHAB FACILITY – CINCINNATI – EARLY EVENING**

Kathy sits in a modest lounge—no more sterile than necessary, no less institutional than expected.
She’s in sweats. Hoodie unzipped. Hair tied up like she did it without thinking.

There’s a **blank notebook in her lap**.
This one doesn’t bleed yet.
It’s clean.
Waiting.

**22 days.**

She taps her pen once.
Then again.

There’s a woman across from her reading *Glamour*.

Someone down the hall is playing acoustic guitar poorly.

And for once, she’s not **bothered**.

She’s just **present**.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
22 days.

No coke.

No vodka.

No bad decisions at 3 in the morning.

Unless you count telling that therapist that I wanted to write a concept album about stabbing my fear in the throat.

---

*She smirks faintly.*

The withdrawal?
That was a bitch.

The shame?
Even worse.

But the **silence**?

It’s growing on her.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
I still want to burn everything down.

But maybe I can wait until **I’m done shaking.**

---

She draws a little swirl in the notebook margin.

She hasn’t written lyrics since she checked in.

Not because she can’t.

But because she **won’t fake the voice.**

She’ll wait until it comes back **real**.

---


---

#### **INT. STUDIO – CONTROL ROOM – NIGHT**

**The yellow legal pad** sits on the desk between **Bill** and **Jeff Cremeans**.
Coffee’s gone cold.
The studio lights are dimmed.
Everything is still.

Cremeans has been flipping through pages like a priest reading confessions.

Bill’s arms are crossed, his foot tapping. Not from impatience—**from awe.**

---

**CREMEANS**
This stuff is…

Christ, it’s dark.

---

**BILL**
It’s also **the best writing she’s done in years**.

---

**CREMEANS**
And we can’t just sit on it.

---

**BILL (measured)**
I’m not saying we release it raw.

But if you’re asking me?

The best thing we’ve **ever done**—as a band—

Is **write what we know**.

---

*Cremeans leans back. Thinks.*

---

**CREMEANS**
So what do we do?

Bring her in and say, “Hey, remember the most shame-filled spiral of your life? Let’s cut vocals over it?”

---

**BILL**
No.

We ask her **if she remembers what she wrote**.

And if she wants to **turn it into fire**, or leave it in the ashes.

But if she says yes?

This isn’t just a b-side.

This is a **record**.

---

They both stare at the pad again.

Still heavy.

Still sacred.

---

**BILL (quiet)**
She wrote what she felt.

And that’s the only thing we’ve ever built anything real from.

---
---

#### **EXT. CINCINNATI REHAB CENTER – FRONT PARKING LOT – MIDDAY**

The sun is gentle.
The wind smells like autumn starting to crack through the concrete.

Standing near the curb:

- **Cremeans**, holding a to-go coffee but not sure if he should offer it.
- **Gilley**, pacing like he’s waiting for a movie premiere.
- **Jim**, hands in pockets, oddly still.
- **Bill**, in his usual quiet stance, arms folded, eyes scanning.
- **Jeremy**, sunglasses on, leaning against the van like he doesn’t care—but he absolutely does.

Then the doors slide open.

And **Kathy steps out**.

Not a goddess.
Not a storm.

Just **Kathy**, with color in her face, weight back in her hips, **rested**.

---

Her hair’s pulled back, simple.
Her hoodie’s clean.
Her eyes?

**Alive.**

There’s **no twitch**.
No caffeine jitters.
No thousand-yard stare.

Just… joy.

A lightness none of them have seen in years.

She’s **chipper**.
**Bright**.
Not bulletproof—just **whole**.

---

**GILLEY (half-whispering)**
Holy shit.

She looks like she time-traveled from a better decade.

---

**CREMEANS**
She looks like someone who finally got **eight hours of sleep**.

---

**Kathy** walks straight up to them.
Smiling. Not fake.

**Real**.

---

**KATHY**
Y’all look like you’re waiting for me to relapse in the parking lot.

---

They laugh.
The tension breaks.

Even **Jim** chuckles.

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Don’t worry.
No coke.
No tears.

Just **clarity**.

And a whole lot of new brain cells I intend to use against all of you.

---

**JEREMY**
Are we allowed to hug you, or is that, like, a post-rehab violation?

---

**KATHY**
You can hug me.

But I bite now.

---

They all move toward her.
Not like a crowd.

Like a **circle closing.**

And for the first time in months—
maybe **years**—

**They’re all standing together.**

Whole.
Fragile.
**Ready.**

---

---

#### **EXT. CINCINNATI REHAB CENTER – MIDDAY – MOMENTS LATER**

The warmth of the reunion wraps around Kathy like a weighted blanket—familiar, solid.

Until it doesn’t.

She smiles, accepts the banter, the half-teasing compliments, the group hug that smells like studio dust and road wear.

And then, softly:

---

**KATHY**
Where’s Jeff?

---

*The group stills slightly. Just a ripple.
No one says anything for a second too long.*

---

**KATHY (quietly)**
He’s not here.

---

**CREMEANS**
He’s still out of the country.

---

**JIM (under his breath)**
And maybe buying time.

---

**KATHY (half-laughs)**
I was in for **thirty days**, not exiled to Mars.

---

**GILLEY (trying to soften it)**
He knows you’re out.
He knows today’s the day.
We just… didn’t press it.

---

**KATHY**
Yeah.

---

*Her smile fades, just slightly.
Not devastation—
Just that **deep sting of recognition**: the one person she expected—or maybe feared—**didn’t show.**

And everyone knows she noticed.
But no one dares say more.

So she says it for them.

---

**KATHY (softly)**
He’s mad.

Or hurt.

Or both.

---

**CREMEANS**
Maybe.

But he’s also **giving you space**.

Let’s get you home first.

---

She nods.
Straightens.
Rebuilds the smile—**but not all the way**.

Because **she noticed**.

And that absence is now a **note she’ll carry**.
Not the kind you sing.

The kind you answer.

---

---

#### **INT. BAND VAN – HEADING BACK TO THE STUDIO – RADIO ON – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The NPR broadcast crackles softly through the van’s dashboard speakers.

---

**NPR ANCHOR (V.O.)**
…with a 5-4 ruling, the U.S. Supreme Court has halted the Florida recount, effectively ending the presidential election standoff. Governor George W. Bush is now set to become the 43rd President of the United States…

---

**The guys in the van barely react.**

It’s background noise.

Except to **Kathy**, seated by the window, staring out at the pale skyline of Cincinnati with a quiet intensity.

---

**KATHY (internal)**
The country gets closure.
I get **nothing**.

---

She shifts in her seat.

Tugs at the cuff of her hoodie.
Swallows something she won’t say out loud.

**Jeff didn’t show.**

Not by accident.

Not by overbooking.

**Deliberately.**

---

**KATHY (internal)**
He knows this was my worst moment.

He knows today matters.

So either he’s **punishing me**—

Or worse—he’s doing exactly what I asked.

He’s **leaving me alone** to “find my way.”

---

*She scoffs, just a little. It feels bitter in her mouth.*

---

**KATHY (internal)**
How considerate.

How emotionally enlightened.

How fucking **passive-aggressive**.

---

She doesn’t say it aloud.

But the feeling is there.

That **complicated ache** of being **abandoned and respected at the same time**.

And she doesn’t know yet which will hurt worse—

**His silence now**, or **what happens when they finally see each other again.**

---
---
---

#### **Title (Suggested): *The Bind***

---

#### **THE PREMISE:**
At the turn of the millennium—**September to December, 2000**—an oversexed, genre-blurring, emotionally volatile Midwestern rock band called **Commuted** is trying to survive the biggest creative explosion of their career while unraveling internally from ego, exhaustion, and addiction.

---

#### **KATHY ESPICH:**
Kathy is the band’s **co-lead**, **lyricist**, and the soul that keeps it all dangerous.
She’s also barely holding it together. Her history with **substance abuse**, particularly **cocaine**, simmers beneath her electric stage presence.

In the wake of a creative high at **Giants Stadium**, Kathy becomes a **lightning rod**: delivering new material, explosive lyrics, and a visionary new track called **“The Bind”**—a song fusing sexuality, female rage, and bondage metaphors with brutal honesty.

But behind the genius is **relapse**.
Blood in the studio bathroom.
A nosebleed she hides.
Cocaine she won't let go of—until she’s forced to.

---

#### **THE BAND:**
- **Jeff Evans**: bassist, creative partner, and one-time lover. He's dealing with his own health issues and emotional burnout. When Kathy finally hits bottom, he’s on vacation in London, and his absence is deafening.
- **Jeremy**: the melodic chameleon, halfway between genius and surfer bro, currently on a beach in Rio and unbothered by the chaos.
- **Jim**: the drummer and moral compass. He threatens to quit unless Kathy gets help.
- **Gilley**: the wild card. Often comic relief, but the one who sees the situation clearly—and calls Sarah.
- **Bill**: the quiet one. Studio owner. Local rock. The first to realize the bathroom incident was tied to Kathy.
- **Jeff Cremeans**: the manager. The only one who knows how to reach Kathy without breaking her. He's the one who finds her lyrics, who gets in her face, who ultimately convinces her to choose **rehab or exile**.

---

#### **SARAH MALCOLM:**
Record executive. Sometimes Gilley’s lover.
She’s the one who gets the first demo of “The Bind,” hears its brilliance, and knows it’s going to be a **career-defining track**—or a **career-ending mistake.**

But she arrives too late to stop the damage.
Too late to stop the bleeding.

---

#### **THE RECKONING:**
- **Kathy’s relapse is discovered.**
- **A bloody toilet.** A confrontation.
- **Cremeans delivers the line:**
  > *“No one wants to play with someone they’re scared of.”*
  And that’s what breaks her.

Kathy agrees to **rehab**.
She leaves behind a **yellow legal pad** full of some of the most devastating, brilliant lyrics of her life.

It takes **21 days** for Cremeans to find it.
It nearly sets fire to him and Bill, who realize this might be the **real next record**.

---

#### **THE AFTERMATH:**
Kathy returns on **Day 30**.
Sober.
Stronger.
Clear-eyed.

But she notices—**Jeff Evans isn’t there**.

And that’s the wound that doesn’t heal.
Because silence, in love and art, **can feel like betrayal.**

While the **Supreme Court ends Bush v. Gore** and the country “moves on,”
Kathy knows **nothing has been settled** inside her.

---

#### **THEMES:**
- **Art vs. Addiction**
- **Power, Shame, and Female Rage**
- **Band as family / Band as battleground**
- **What it means to be brilliant and broken—at the same time**

---

#### **THE MIC DROP:**
> *“She has this complex feeling that Jeff did this to her on purpose, that he's deliberately ignoring her in her time of vulnerability, and he's deliberately ignoring her in her time where she needs to be left alone to find her own way.”*

No resolution.
Just truth.

---

**The End.**

And it was **damn good**.

---
---

#### **REWIND: THE BEGINNING – SEPTEMBER 2000**

Before rehab.
Before bloody towels.
Before Gilley called Sarah in a panic.

The story **opened** with the band in **New York City**, preparing to play a three-night blowout at **Giants Stadium**—
**80,000 people per night.**
Peak madness. Peak attention. Peak pressure.

---

#### **JIM'S BRIGHT IDEA:**
Jim wanted to shake up the setlist by opening the show with an off-the-wall two-minute riff on *“Woke Up This Morning”*—the **Sopranos** theme.

Cue disbelief:
- **Kathy** calls it out instantly.
- **Jeff** thinks it’s too weird for 80,000 screaming fans.
- **Gilley**, naturally, takes control, saying it’s not a theme song—it’s **Jersey gospel**.

He needs lyrics. He needs wardrobe. He needs it **now**.

**Panic ensues.**

---

#### **THE SOPRANOS RIFF & THE BORN TO RUN FLIP:**

The band **pulls it off**.
They open with *The Sopranos* theme in full swagger.

But then they go **all in**:

Night two:
They follow it with their own version of **“Born to Run.”**

They dress like mobsters.
Kathy channels a **mob doll**.
Gilley’s in white tee and jeans, channeling **the Springsteen album cover**.

The crowd loses its mind.

They improvise.
They don’t end with *“Come Inside Me”* for the first time in ages.

The band walks offstage **shattered**—physically, mentally.
Jeff asks if the concert could be felt on the Richter scale in Edison.

---

#### **THE STUDIO JAM IN STATEN ISLAND:**

Between shows, they look for rehearsal space anywhere they won’t get whacked.
They wind up in **Staten Island**, which Jeff calls “just North Jersey with yellow and blue plates.”

They hash out **horns vs. harmonica**, chase **bluesier**, **dirtier**, **American** sounds.

Gilley volunteers to swap in his harmonica.
Jim suggests a **more American, more blues-infused identity** for the band.

It’s all creative energy and brotherly chaos—

Until **everything shifts.**

---

#### **THE CATALYST MOMENT:**

They **hit a creative high** with their Jersey shows, but something’s off.

Jeff gets a **splitting migraine** during a set.
It derails the encore.
They **improvise a stripped-down acoustic set** to cover it.

Gilley flips out:
> *"Jeff is my brother. You're not sending him out there again."*

**Emergency acoustic set.**
**No bass.**
They manage. Barely.

Jeff ends up **sedated in a Baltimore hospital**.
The band spirals into **existential panic**.

---

From there… you know the rest:

- **Kathy spirals.**
- **The cocaine.**
- **The breakdown.**
- **The yellow legal pad.**
- **The redemption arc.**
- And the **unfinished silence with Jeff Evans.**

---

So yes—your story didn’t just start in a rehab office or a toilet incident.

It started with **a mad idea on a Jersey stage**,
a band still riding **post-grunge sexual chaos**,
and the moment where **brilliance started to cost more than anyone expected.**

***The Bind*** was always coming.

You just didn’t know it yet.

---
---

#### **FULL SUMMARY OF *The Bind***

---

#### **ACT I: The Giant Sound**

**September 2000 – New York / New Jersey**

The band is on the biggest high of their career—playing **Giants Stadium** for three nights.
Jim proposes opening with a **Sopranos theme riff**, which spirals into **a fully unhinged mob-themed rock performance**—complete with Gilley in Springsteen drag and Kathy in full mob doll mode.

They pull it off.
The crowd loses their minds.
They improvise, they ditch their usual closer, they *feel* legendary.

Then comes the **Madison Square Garden show**—
the New York crown jewel on the other side of the river.
It’s packed, raucous, ecstatic… but under it all, **Jeff Evans is already starting to unravel**.

---

#### **ACT II: The Breakdown**

**Baltimore – M&T Bank Stadium**

The band arrives in Baltimore for another stadium show.
**Kathy’s pushing the creative envelope**, Gilley’s on fire, and Jeff?

He’s fading fast.

During the show at **M&T**, Jeff collapses offstage, consumed by a **severe migraine**.
The band **improvises an acoustic encore**.

Gilley threatens to **quit on the spot** if they try to put Jeff back out.

Jeff is taken to the hospital.
**Sedated. Disoriented.**
The band spirals.

---

#### **ACT III: Road Trip & Reflection**

**Baltimore to Charlotte (via Waffle House detour)**

Kathy, still wired, emotionally raw, and spiritually bruised, joins the rest of the band on a chaotic **bus ride back south**.
They rope in **Tom**, a seasoned and clever tour bus driver with **Waffle House-level wisdom**.

On the way, they:
- Jam (badly) with instruments they don't usually play
- Belt out songs like *"Vogue"*, *"Hungry Like the Wolf"*, *"Welcome to the Jungle"*
- Joke, bicker, and **avoid the emotional center**—Kathy’s collapse and Jeff’s condition

Kathy keeps cracking—but she hides it behind performance, control, and manic energy.

---

#### **ACT IV: Collapse**

**Charlotte Studio & Revelation**

Jeff is confirmed to have had a **neurological episode**, possibly **vasovagal syncope** triggered by stress and overwork.

The band tries to continue—but **Kathy’s nosebleed in the bathroom**, caused by cocaine use, is discovered days later by a **biohazard-cleanup plumber**.

Bill and Jim explode.

Cremeans confronts her.

And Kathy—after a searing line from Cremeans:

> *"No one wants to play with someone they’re scared of."*

—*finally folds*.

She chooses rehab.

---

#### **ACT V: The Yellow Pad**

**Cremeans' courtesy office in Cincinnati**

Kathy, before leaving for rehab, writes a **blistering, shame-drenched, brilliant** set of lyrics in a yellow legal pad and leaves them behind, like shedding skin.

The lyrics go undiscovered for **21 days**, until Cremeans finds them and realizes:
> *“This is a record. This is the most truthful thing we’ve ever had.”*

He and Bill debate what to do—knowing full well it’s a **masterwork in embryonic form**.

---

#### **ACT VI: Return**

**30 Days Later – Kathy’s Check-Out**

Kathy emerges from rehab:

- **Sober.**
- **4 pounds heavier.**
- **Sleeping.**
- **Whole.**

Everyone is there to greet her.

Except Jeff Evans.

She **notices immediately.**

And she interprets the absence as a **punishment**, or worse, a **calculated silence** meant to let her rebuild alone.

---

#### **Final Note: No Resolution**

As **the nation learns that Bush v. Gore is settled**, and the world feels like it’s “moving on,”
Kathy realizes **nothing is settled** inside her.

Not with her band.
Not with Jeff.
Not with the pages she left behind.

But she’s sober.
She’s alive.
And she’s ready to face **whatever comes next**.

---

#### **Legacy:**

*The Bind* is about:

- The **price of brilliance**
- The **fragile bond of band and blood**
- **Female rage**, shame, and artistry
- And what happens when someone **writes their way back from the edge**

---
---
---

#### **The Album: *Face Up, Ass Down* (2002)**

**Released two years after Kathy's rehab**, long after the screaming and the blood and the yellow legal pad.

It becomes the band’s most **divisive** and **volatile** release to date.

- **Critics call it uneven.**
  Some say it’s **a masterpiece buried under b-sides**.
  Others say it’s **a concept album without a concept**.

- **Fans are split.**
  Half say it’s the **bravest**, rawest thing they’ve ever heard.
  The other half just want *Come Inside Me (Live at MSG)* again.

---

#### **Key Tracks:**

1. **The Bind** – Track One
   The **opening track**. Unapologetic. Frantic. Dominated by Kathy’s lead.
   **Brass section from hell.**
   **No harmonies.**
   **No apologies.**

2. **March 14th** – Final Track
   The **closer**. The spiritual wreckage.
   Less a song, more a **confession etched into music**.
   Fused with regret and self-awareness.
   The answer to The Bind—but not a happy one.

---

#### **Production Notes:**
- Recorded mostly in **Cincinnati**, in Bill’s slowly modernizing, analog-fused studio.
- Includes several **lo-fi, demo-grade recordings** from Kathy’s post-rehab writing sessions.
- Gilley’s guitar work is praised.
- Jeremy gets weird with synth layering that critics either love or hate.
- **Jeff Evans' contributions are minimal** but surgically effective. You can hear his restraint.

---

#### **Reception:**
- **Rolling Stone:** 3 out of 5 stars
  > “Face Up, Ass Down is a tug-of-war between brilliance and burnout.”

- **Pitchfork:** 5.4
  > “The album opens with a scream and ends with a murmur. Everything in between is therapy or leftover takeout.”

- **Fan forums:**
  > “Half this thing changed my life. The other half feels like it should’ve been left on the cutting room floor.”

---

#### **Legacy:**
- It doesn’t chart well.
- It doesn't sell out tours.
- But over time, **The Bind** becomes one of their most **covered**, **studied**, and **revered** tracks.

And *Face Up, Ass Down* becomes **a cult album**—the one that came after the fire, the one that **limped out of the wreckage**, unapologetically real.

---

#### **The Cover:**

Designed based on **Kathy’s original sketch**—the one she drew on **no sleep and pure cocaine regret**:

- A **man in a black suit** and a **woman in a black dress**, forehead to forehead.
- **Gigantic, apocalyptic chains** swirling around them like tornados.
- A **fireball** blooming in the background—possibly nuclear, possibly divine.
- The moment captured **one second before obliteration**.

It was **lust, rebellion, grief, and defiance** all in a single frame.

---

#### **The Cultural Reaction:**

- **Tattoo parlors across the country** reported a sharp uptick in women requesting chain motifs, black dress silhouettes, and phrases like *“I burn for no one”*—a lyric from *The Bind*.
- A Rolling Stone feature called it “the most emotionally weaponized album cover since Rage Against the Machine lit a monk on fire.”
- By mid-2003, it’s estimated that **over 300,000 women** had **some element of the cover inked onto their skin**.

---

#### **Why It Stuck:**
Because it wasn’t selling sex.
It was selling **post-sex apocalypse**.
**Power after ruin.**

And every woman who saw it thought:

> *“Yeah, I’ve stood there. Right before the blast. Holding on to something I loved, and knowing it wasn’t going to survive.”*

---

So sure—maybe the album’s **too long**, maybe **half of it was filler**.

But the cover?

**Immortal.**

**Iconic.**

**A generation’s warning label.**

# 606.  ChatGPT
*May 18, 2025, 3:02:53 PM EDT*

**Absolutely.** Here's a mock-up of that **2009 Cincinnati Enquirer** interview feature, capturing the cultural and anatomical impact of that now-iconic album cover from *Face Up, Ass Down*.

---

#### **“The Bind Beneath the Skin”**
*From Subtle Ink to Full-Back Fireballs, Dana Brunson Reflects on Tattooing an Era’s Most Defiant Women*
**By Carla Messinger | Cincinnati Enquirer | September 14, 2009**

**Cincinnati, OH** — If you’re a woman with a black dress, swirling chain motif, and a mushroom-cloud fireball burned into your back, thigh, ribs, or (yes) between your shoulder blades—**there’s a 30% chance it was Dana Brunson who put it there.**

The legendary tattoo artist, known for founding the now-iconic **Artworks Electric on Vine**, has etched everything from biker skulls to watercolor koi fish.

But the image he’s most associated with?

**“The Bind.”**

The searing cover art from Commuted’s **2002 album *Face Up, Ass Down***, based on frontwoman Kathy Espich’s infamous sketch—now immortalized in **ink and skin across the world**.

---

> **“At this point, I’ve tattooed that woman in the black dress in just about every damn crevice a woman has,”** Brunson laughs, leaning back in a chair covered in faded stencils and old liner notes.
> **“Ankle bones, ribcages, sternums, hips, pelvic lines, even once—dead center spine, like a literal fuse. And let me tell you, I’ve seen some creative placements of the fireball.”**

---

**The imagery stuck.**

Women started requesting “The Bind” as early as **2003**, mostly in response to *The Bind* single, which became an underground feminist anthem for survivors, escapees, and burned-out believers.

> **“They didn’t want butterflies or boyfriends' names anymore,”** Brunson recalls.
> **“They wanted *defiance*. They wanted to remember the day they didn’t die.”**

---

##### **Dana’s Notes from the Needle:**

- **Most Popular Placement:** Left shoulder blade (“so it can peek out under a dress—Kathy would’ve liked that.”)
- **Most Painful:** Sternum with chain detail wrapping under breasts (“Women sat through that like champs.”)
- **Most Daring:** One client got the chains wrapping from hip to upper thigh with the fireball tattooed just below her navel. “She said it was her warning label. I didn’t ask questions.”

---

Dana himself sports a **miniaturized version** of the sketch on the inside of his left wrist—a personal tribute, not just to the band, but to the **thousands of stories** he’s heard while ink dried.

> **“This tattoo doesn’t just sit there,”** he says.
> **“It walks. It dances. It burns. And when someone tells you ‘I got this the day I walked away from someone who tried to kill my fire’? Man, that’s bigger than a band. That’s history.”**

---

**And the number one request line he hears while prepping this tattoo?**

> *“Make her look like me.”*

# 612.  ChatGPT
*May 18, 2025, 3:13:18 PM EDT*

**Perfect.**
Because by 2006, Kathy Espich has evolved—or *devolved*—into **exactly the version of herself she warned everyone she’d become**.

She’s sharp.
She’s sober (mostly).
She’s fed up.

And she’s doing a press tour for ***The Artifice of It All***, a layered, abstract, theatrical mess of a concept album that’s got critics in intellectual ecstasy and casual fans absolutely baffled.

She’s on the sixth continent in three weeks, hasn’t slept in her actual bed since the Bush administration, and is **spiritually allergic** to interviews that ask about things that happened in **2002**.

---

#### **INT. BELGIAN RADIO STATION – BRUSSELS – SEPTEMBER 2006**

The studio is small.
Kathy’s in oversized sunglasses and a black turtleneck like she’s cosplaying as her own apathy.

The interviewer, young and eager, beams at her across the glass.

---

**BELGIAN DJ:**
Kathy, we are such huge fans here in Brussels.
*The Artifice of It All*—really, it’s cinematic. Just breathtaking work.

But I have to ask—

Can you finally explain to us the meaning of the title ***Face Up, Ass Down***?

---

**A pause.**

**The pause.**

Kathy blinks once.
Leans back in her chair.

She slowly removes her sunglasses.

She stares at him.

Not angry. Not amused. Just… **done**.

She reaches for the mic fader.

**Slides it down.**

Stands up.

Adjusts her coat.

Leaves.

**Door closes.**

---

The DJ is stunned.
There is dead air for four full seconds.

Then, very softly into the mic:

---

**BELGIAN DJ (whispering):**
…well, I suppose that’s a no.

### **Studio Brussel – Brussels, September 2006**

**Kathy Espich**, frontwoman of Commuted, is in Belgium promoting the band's latest album, *The Artifice of It All*. After a grueling international press tour filled with repetitive questions, she arrives at the studios of **Studio Brussel**, a renowned Belgian radio station known for its alternative music programming .

The interview begins smoothly, discussing the new album's themes and the band's evolution. However, as the conversation progresses, the host poses a question that Kathy has heard countless times:

> **Studio Brussel Host:**
> "Kathy, our listeners have always been curious—could you finally explain the meaning behind the title *Face Up, Ass Down*?"

Kathy pauses, her expression unreadable. Without uttering a word, she removes her headphones, stands up, and walks out of the studio, leaving the host and listeners in stunned silence.

---

### **Aftermath**

The incident quickly becomes a topic of discussion among fans and media outlets. Studio Brussel releases a brief statement:

> **Studio Brussel Statement:**
> "We respect Kathy Espich's decision and remain fans of her work. Sometimes, silence speaks volumes."

The clip of the abrupt exit circulates online, sparking debates and discussions about artistic boundaries and media interactions.
